See the documentation for the InputValue\n    36→\t// type for more information on how to correctly populate this.\n    37→\t//\n    38→\t// During the apply phase it's only valid to specify values for input\n    39→\t// values that were declared as ephemeral, because all other input\n    40→\t// values must retain the values that were specified during planning.\n    41→\tSetVariables InputValues\n    42→}\n    43→\n    44→// ApplyOpts creates an [ApplyOpts] with copies of all of the elements that\n    45→// are expected to propagate from plan to apply when planning and applying\n    46→// in the same process.\n    47→//\n    48→// In practice planning and applying are often separated into two different\n    49→// executions, in which case callers must retain enough information between\n    50→// plan and apply to construct an equivalent [ApplyOpts] themselves without\n    51→// using this function. This is here mainly for convenient internal use such\n    52→// as in test cases.\n    53→func (po *PlanOpts) ApplyOpts() *ApplyOpts {\n    54→\treturn &ApplyOpts{\n    55→\t\tExternalProviders: po.ExternalProviders,\n    56→\t}\n    57→}\n    58→\n    59→// Apply performs the actions described by the given Plan object and returns\n    60→// the resulting updated state.\n    61→//\n    62→// The given configuration *must* be the same configuration that was passed\n    63→// earlier to Context.Plan in order to create this plan.\n    64→//\n    65→// Even if the returned diagnostics contains errors, Apply always returns the\n    66→// resulting state which is likely to have been partially-updated.\n    67→//\n    68→// The [opts] argument may be nil to indicate that no special options are\n    69→// required. In that case, Apply will use a default set of options. Some\n    70→// options in [PlanOpts] when creating a plan must be echoed with equivalent\n    71→// settings during apply, so leaving opts as nil might not be valid for\n    72→// certain combinations of plan-time options.\n    73→func (c *Context) Apply(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    74→\tstate, _, diags := c.ApplyAndEval(plan, config, opts)\n    75→\treturn state, diags\n    76→}\n    77→\n    78→// ApplyAndEval is like [Context.Apply] except that it additionally makes a\n    79→// best effort to return a [lang.Scope] which can evaluate expressions in the\n    80→// root module based on the content of the new state.\n    81→//\n    82→// The scope will be nil if the apply process doesn't complete successfully\n    83→// enough to produce a valid evaluation scope. If the returned state is nil\n    84→// then the scope will always be nil, but it's also possible for the scope\n    85→// to be nil even when the state isn't, if the apply didn't complete enough for\n    86→// the evaluation scope to produce consistent results.\n    87→func (c *Context) ApplyAndEval(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    88→\tdefer c.acquireRun(\"apply\")()\n    89→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n    90→\n    91→\tif plan == nil {\n    92→\t\tpanic(\"cannot apply nil plan\")\n    93→\t}\n    94→\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Building and walking apply graph for %s plan\", plan.UIMode)\n    95→\n    96→\tif opts == nil {\n    97→\t\topts = &ApplyOpts{}\n    98→\t}\n    99→\n   100→\tif plan.Errored {\n   101→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   102→\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n   103→\t\t\t\"Cannot apply failed plan\",\n   104→\t\t\t`The given plan is incomplete due to errors during planning, and so it cannot be applied.`,\n   105→\t\t))\n   106→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   107→\t}\n   108→\tif !plan.Applyable {\n   109→\t\tif plan.Changes.Empty() {\n   110→\t\t\t// If a plan is not applyable but it didn't have any errors then that\n   111→\t\t\t// suggests it was a \"no-op\" plan, which doesn't really do any\n   112→\t\t\t// harm to apply, so we'll just do it but leave ourselves a note\n   113→\t\t\t// in the trace log in case it ends up relevant to a bug report.\n   114→\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Applying a no-op plan\")\n   115→\t\t} else {\n   116→\t\t\t// This situation isn't something we expect, since our own rules\n   117→\t\t\t// for what \"applyable\" means make this scenario impossible. We'll\n   118→\t\t\t// reject it on the assumption that something very strange is\n   119→\t\t\t// going on. and so better to halt than do something incorrect.\n   120→\t\t\t// This error message is generic and useless because we don't\n   121→\t\t\t// expect anyone to ever see it in normal use.\n   122→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   123→\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n   124→\t\t\t\t\"Cannot apply non-applyable plan\",\n   125→\t\t\t\t`The given plan is not applyable. If this seems like a bug in Terraform, then please report it!`,\n   126→\t\t\t))\n   127→\t\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   128→\t\t}\n   129→\t}\n   130→\n   131→\t// The caller must provide values for all of the \"apply-time variables\"\n   132→\t// mentioned in the plan, and for no others because the others come from\n   133→\t// the plan itself.\n   134→\t// Apply-time variable check handled by graph walk validation.\n   135→\n   136→\tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n   137→\t\t// Import is a no-op change during an apply (all the real action happens during the plan) but we'd\n   138→\t\t// like to show some helpful output that mirrors the way we show other changes.\n   139→\t\tif rc.Importing != nil {\n   140→\t\t\thookResourceID := HookResourceIdentity{\n   141→\t\t\t\tAddr:         rc.Addr,\n   142→\t\t\t\tProviderAddr: rc.ProviderAddr.Provider,\n   143→\t\t\t}\n   144→\t\t\tfor _, h := range c.hooks {\n   145→\t\t\t\t// In future, we may need to call PostApplyImport separately elsewhere in the apply\n   146→\t\t\t\t// operation. For now, though, we'll call Pre and Post hooks together.\n   147→\t\t\t\th.PreApplyImport(hookResourceID, *rc.Importing)\n   148→\t\t\t\th.PostApplyImport(hookResourceID, *rc.Importing)\n   149→\t\t\t}\n   150→\t\t}\n   151→\t}\n   152→\n   153→\tgraph, operation, moreDiags := c.applyGraph(plan, config, opts, true)\n   154→\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   155→\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n   156→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   157→\t}\n   158→\n   159→\tmoreDiags = checkExternalProviders(config, plan, nil, opts.ExternalProviders)\n   160→\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   161→\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n   162→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   163→\t}\n   164→\n   165→\tschemas, schemaDiags := c.Schemas(config, plan.PriorState)\n   166→\tdiags = diags.Append(schemaDiags)\n   167→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   168→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   169→\t}\n   170→\n   171→\tchanges, err := plan.Changes.Decode(schemas)\n   172→\tif err != nil {\n   173→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(err)\n   174→\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n   175→\t}\n   176→\n   177→\tworkingState := plan.PriorState.DeepCopy()\n   178→\twalker, walkDiags := c.walk(graph, operation, &graphWalkOpts{\n   179→\t\tConfig:                  config,\n   180→\t\tInputState:              workingState,\n   181→\t\tChanges:                 changes,\n   182→\t\tOverrides:               plan.Overrides,\n   183→\t\tExternalProviderConfigs: opts.ExternalProviders,\n   184→\n   185→\t\tDeferralAllowed: true,\n   186→\n   187→\t\t// We need to propagate the check results from the plan phase,\n   188→\t\t// because that will tell us which checkable objects we're expecting\n   189→\t\t// to see updated results from during the apply step.\n   190→\t\tPlanTimeCheckResults: plan.Checks,\n   191→\n   192→\t\t// We also want to propagate the timestamp from the plan file.\n   193→\t\tPlanTimeTimestamp: plan.Timestamp,\n   194→\n   195→\t\tProviderFuncResults: providers.NewFunctionResultsTable(plan.ProviderFunctionResults),\n   196→\t})\n   197→\tdiags = diags.Append(walker.NonFatalDiagnostics)\n   198→\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n   199→\n   200→\t// After the walk is finished, we capture a simplified snapshot of the\n   201→\t// check result data as part of the new state.\n   202→\twalker.State.RecordCheckResults(walker.Checks)\n   203→\n   204→\tnewState := walker.State.Close()\n   205→\tif plan.UIMode == plans.DestroyMode && !diags.HasErrors() {\n   206→\t\t// NOTE: This is a vestigial violation of the rule that we mustn't\n   207→\t\t// use plan.UIMode to affect apply-time behavior.\n   208→\t\t// We ideally ought to just call newState.PruneResourceHusks\n   209→\t\t// unconditionally here, but we historically didn't and haven't yet\n   210→\t\t// verified that it'd be safe to do so.\n   211→\t\tnewState.PruneResourceHusks()\n   212→\t}\n   213→\n   214→\tif len(plan.TargetAddrs) > 0 {\n   215→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   216→\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n   217→\t\t\t\"Applied changes may be incomplete\",\n   218→\t\t\t`The plan was created with the -target option in effect, so some changes requested in the configuration may have been ignored and the output values may not be fully updated. Run the following command to verify that no other changes are pending:\n   219→    terraform plan\n   220→\n   221→Note that the -target option is not suitable for routine use, and is provided only for exceptional situations such as recovering from errors or mistakes, or when Terraform specifically suggests to use it as part of an error message.`,\n   222→\t\t))\n   223→\t}\n   224→\n   225→\t// FIXME: we cannot check for an empty plan for refresh-only, because root\n   226→\t// outputs are always stored as changes. The final condition of the state\n   227→\t// also depends on some cleanup which happens during the apply walk. It\n   228→\t// would probably make more sense if applying a refresh-only plan were\n   229→\t// simply just returning the planned state and checks, but some extra\n   230→\t// cleanup is going to be needed to make the plan state match what apply\n   231→\t// would do. For now we can copy the checks over which were overwritten\n   232→\t// during the apply walk.\n   233→\t// Despite the intent of UIMode, it must still be used for apply-time\n   234→\t// differences in destroy plans too, so we can make use of that here as\n   235→\t// well.\n   236→\tif plan.UIMode == plans.RefreshOnlyMode {\n   237→\t\tnewState.CheckResults = plan.Checks.DeepCopy()\n   238→\t}\n   239→\n   240→\t// The caller also gets access to an expression evaluation scope in the\n   241→\t// root module, in case it needs to extract other information using\n   242→\t// expressions, like in \"terraform console\" or the test harness.\n   243→\tevalScope := evalScopeFromGraphWalk(walker, addrs.RootModuleInstance)\n   244→\n   245→\treturn newState, evalScope, diags\n   246→}\n   247→\n   248→func checkApplyTimeVariables(needed collections.Set[string], gotValues InputValues, config *configs.Config) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n   249→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   250→\tfor name := range needed.All() {\n   251→\t\tif vv, exists := gotValues[name]; !exists || vv.Value == cty.NilVal || vv.Value.IsNull() {\n   252→\t\t\t// This error message assumes that the only possible reason for\n   253→\t\t\t// an apply-time variable is because the variable is ephemeral,\n   254→\t\t\t// which is true at the time of writing. This error message might\n   255→\t\t\t// need to be generalized if we introduce other reasons for\n   256→\t\t\t// apply-time variables in future.\n   257→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n   258→\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n   259→\t\t\t\t\"No value for required variable\",\n   260→\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"The ephemeral input variable %q was set during the plan phase, and so must also be set during the apply phase.\", name),\n   261→\t\t\t))\n   262→\t\t}\n   263→\t}\n   264→\tfor name := range gotValues {\n   265→\t\tif !needed.Has(name) {\n   266→\t\t\t// We'll treat this a little differently depending on whether\n   267→\t\t\t// the variable is declared as ephemeral or not.\n   268→\t\t\tif vc, ok := config.Module.Variables[name]; ok {\n   329→\t\t\tcontinue\n   330→\t\t}\n   331→\t\tvariables[name] = &InputValue{\n   332→\t\t\tValue:      cty.NilVal,\n   333→\t\t\tSourceType: ValueFromPlan,\n   334→\t\t}\n   335→\t}\n   336→\n   337→\toperation := walkApply\n   338→\tif plan.UIMode == plans.DestroyMode {\n   339→\t\t// FIXME: Due to differences in how objects must be handled in the\n   340→\t\t// graph and evaluated during a complete destroy, we must continue to\n   341→\t\t// use plans.DestroyMode to switch on this behavior. If all objects\n   342→\t\t// which require special destroy handling can be tracked in the plan,\n   343→\t\t// then this switch will no longer be needed and we can remove the\n   344→\t\t// walkDestroy operation mode.\n   345→\t\t// TODO: Audit that and remove walkDestroy as an operation mode.\n   346→\t\toperation = walkDestroy\n   347→\t}\n   348→\n   349→\tvar externalProviderConfigs (&ApplyGraphBuilder{\n   355→\t\tConfig:                  config,\n   356→\t\tChanges:                 plan.Changes,\n   357→\t\tDeferredChanges:         plan.DeferredResources,\n   358→\t\tState:                   plan.PriorState,\n   359→\t\tRootVariableValues:      variables,\n   360→\t\tExternalProviderConfigs: externalProviderConfigs,\n   361→\t\tPlugins:                 c.plugins,\n   362→\t\tTargets:                 plan.TargetAddrs,\n   363→\t\tForceReplace:            plan.ForceReplaceAddrs,\n   364→\t\tOperation:               operation,\n   365→\t\tExternalReferences:      plan.ExternalReferences,\n   366→\t\tOverrides:               plan.Overrides,\n   367→\t}).Build(addrs.RootModuleInstance)\n   368→\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   369→\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n   370→\t\treturn nil, walkApply, diags\n   371→\t}\n   372→\n   373→\treturn graph, operation, diags\n   374→}\n   375→\n   376→// ApplyGraphForUI is a last vestage of graphs in the public interface of\n   377→// Context (as opposed to graphs as an implementation detail) intended only for\n   378→// use by the \"terraform graph\" command when asked to render an apply-time\n   379→// graph.\n   380→//\n   381→// The result of this is intended only for rendering ot the user as a dot\n   382→// graph, and so may change in future in order to make the result more useful\n   383→// in that context, even if drifts away from the physical graph that Terraform\n   384→// Core currently uses as an implementation detail of applying.\n   385→func (c *Context) ApplyGraphForUI(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   386→\t// For now though, this really is just the internal graph, confusing\n   387→\t// implementation details and all.\n   388→\n   389→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   390→\n   391→\tgraph, _, moreDiags := c.applyGraph(plan, config, nil, false)\n   392→\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   393→\treturn graph, diags\n See the documentation for the InputValue\n\t// type for more information on how to correctly populate this.\n\t//\n\t// During the apply phase it's only valid to specify values for input\n\t// values that were declared as ephemeral, because all other input\n\t// values must retain the values that were specified during planning.\n\tSetVariables InputValues\n}\n\n// ApplyOpts creates an [ApplyOpts] with copies of all of the elements that\n// are expected to propagate from plan to apply when planning and applying\n// in the same process.\n//\n// In practice planning and applying are often separated into two different\n// executions, in which case callers must retain enough information between\n// plan and apply to construct an equivalent [ApplyOpts] themselves without\n// using this function. This is here mainly for convenient internal use such\n// as in test cases.\nfunc (po *PlanOpts) ApplyOpts() *ApplyOpts {\n\treturn &ApplyOpts{\n\t\tExternalProviders: po.ExternalProviders,\n\t}\n}\n\n// Apply performs the actions described by the given Plan object and returns\n// the resulting updated state.\n//\n// The given configuration *must* be the same configuration that was passed\n// earlier to Context.Plan in order to create this plan.\n//\n// Even if the returned diagnostics contains errors, Apply always returns the\n// resulting state which is likely to have been partially-updated.\n//\n// The [opts] argument may be nil to indicate that no special options are\n// required. In that case, Apply will use a default set of options. Some\n// options in [PlanOpts] when creating a plan must be echoed with equivalent\n// settings during apply, so leaving opts as nil might not be valid for\n// certain combinations of plan-time options.\nfunc (c *Context) Apply(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tstate, _, diags := c.ApplyAndEval(plan, config, opts)\n\treturn state, diags\n}\n\n// ApplyAndEval is like [Context.Apply] except that it additionally makes a\n// best effort to return a [lang.Scope] which can evaluate expressions in the\n// root module based on the content of the new state.\n//\n// The scope will be nil if the apply process doesn't complete successfully\n// enough to produce a valid evaluation scope. If the returned state is nil\n// then the scope will always be nil, but it's also possible for the scope\n// to be nil even when the state isn't, if the apply didn't complete enough for\n// the evaluation scope to produce consistent results.\nfunc (c *Context) ApplyAndEval(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tdefer c.acquireRun(\"apply\")()\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tif plan == nil {\n\t\tpanic(\"cannot apply nil plan\")\n\t}\n\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] Building and walking apply graph for %s plan\", plan.UIMode)\n\n\tif opts == nil {\n\t\topts = &ApplyOpts{}\n\t}\n\n\tif plan.Errored {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\"Cannot apply failed plan\",\n\t\t\t`The given plan is incomplete due to errors during planning, and so it cannot be applied.`,\n\t\t))\n\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t}\n\tif !plan.Applyable {\n\t\tif plan.Changes.Empty() {\n\t\t\t// If a plan is not applyable but it didn't have any errors then that\n\t\t\t// suggests it was a \"no-op\" plan, which doesn't really do any\n\t\t\t// harm to apply, so we'll just do it but leave ourselves a note\n\t\t\t// in the trace log in case it ends up relevant to a bug report.\n\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] Applying a no-op plan\")\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t// This situation isn't something we expect, since our own rules\n\t\t\t// for what \"applyable\" means make this scenario impossible. We'll\n\t\t\t// reject it on the assumption that something very strange is\n\t\t\t// going on. and so better to halt than do something incorrect.\n\t\t\t// This error message is generic and useless because we don't\n\t\t\t// expect anyone to ever see it in normal use.\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\t\"Cannot apply non-applyable plan\",\n\t\t\t\t`The given plan is not applyable. If this seems like a bug in Terraform, then please report it!`,\n\t\t\t))\n\t\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// The caller must provide values for all of the \"apply-time variables\"\n\t// mentioned in the plan, and for no others because the others come from\n\t// the plan itself.\n\t// Apply-time variable check handled by graph walk validation.\n\n\tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n\t\t// Import is a no-op change during an apply (all the real action happens during the plan) but we'd\n\t\t// like to show some helpful output that mirrors the way we show other changes.\n\t\tif rc.Importing != nil {\n\t\t\thookResourceID := HookResourceIdentity{\n\t\t\t\tAddr:         rc.Addr,\n\t\t\t\tProviderAddr: rc.ProviderAddr.Provider,\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tfor _, h := range c.hooks {\n\t\t\t\t// In future, we may need to call PostApplyImport separately elsewhere in the apply\n\t\t\t\t// operation. For now, though, we'll call Pre and Post hooks together.\n\t\t\t\th.PreApplyImport(hookResourceID, *rc.Importing)\n\t\t\t\th.PostApplyImport(hookResourceID, *rc.Importing)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tgraph, operation, moreDiags := c.applyGraph(plan, config, opts, true)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t}\n\n\tmoreDiags = checkExternalProviders(config, plan, nil, opts.ExternalProviders)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t}\n\n\tschemas, schemaDiags := c.Schemas(config, plan.PriorState)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(schemaDiags)\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t}\n\n\tchanges, err := plan.Changes.Decode(schemas)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(err)\n\t\treturn nil, nil, diags\n\t}\n\n\tworkingState := plan.PriorState.DeepCopy()\n\twalker, walkDiags := c.walk(graph, operation, &graphWalkOpts{\n\t\tConfig:                  config,\n\t\tInputState:              workingState,\n\t\tChanges:                 changes,\n\t\tOverrides:               plan.Overrides,\n\t\tExternalProviderConfigs: opts.ExternalProviders,\n\n\t\tDeferralAllowed: true,\n\n\t\t// We need to propagate the check results from the plan phase,\n\t\t// because that will tell us which checkable objects we're expecting\n\t\t// to see updated results from during the apply step.\n\t\tPlanTimeCheckResults: plan.Checks,\n\n\t\t// We also want to propagate the timestamp from the plan file.\n\t\tPlanTimeTimestamp: plan.Timestamp,\n\n\t\tProviderFuncResults: providers.NewFunctionResultsTable(plan.ProviderFunctionResults),\n\t})\n\tdiags = diags.Append(walker.NonFatalDiagnostics)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(walkDiags)\n\n\t// After the walk is finished, we capture a simplified snapshot of the\n\t// check result data as part of the new state.\n\twalker.State.RecordCheckResults(walker.Checks)\n\n\tnewState := walker.State.Close()\n\tif plan.UIMode == plans.DestroyMode && !diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// NOTE: This is a vestigial violation of the rule that we mustn't\n\t\t// use plan.UIMode to affect apply-time behavior.\n\t\t// We ideally ought to just call newState.PruneResourceHusks\n\t\t// unconditionally here, but we historically didn't and haven't yet\n\t\t// verified that it'd be safe to do so.\n\t\tnewState.PruneResourceHusks()\n\t}\n\n\tif len(plan.TargetAddrs) > 0 {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\ttfdiags.Warning,\n\t\t\t\"Applied changes may be incomplete\",\n\t\t\t`The plan was created with the -target option in effect, so some changes requested in the configuration may have been ignored and the output values may not be fully updated. Run the following command to verify that no other changes are pending:\n    terraform plan\n\nNote that the -target option is not suitable for routine use, and is provided only for exceptional situations such as recovering from errors or mistakes, or when Terraform specifically suggests to use it as part of an error message.`,\n\t\t))\n\t}\n\n\t// FIXME: we cannot check for an empty plan for refresh-only, because root\n\t// outputs are always stored as changes. The final condition of the state\n\t// also depends on some cleanup which happens during the apply walk. It\n\t// would probably make more sense if applying a refresh-only plan were\n\t// simply just returning the planned state and checks, but some extra\n\t// cleanup is going to be needed to make the plan state match what apply\n\t// would do. For now we can copy the checks over which were overwritten\n\t// during the apply walk.\n\t// Despite the intent of UIMode, it must still be used for apply-time\n\t// differences in destroy plans too, so we can make use of that here as\n\t// well.\n\tif plan.UIMode == plans.RefreshOnlyMode {\n\t\tnewState.CheckResults = plan.Checks.DeepCopy()\n\t}\n\n\t// The caller also gets access to an expression evaluation scope in the\n\t// root module, in case it needs to extract other information using\n\t// expressions, like in \"terraform console\" or the test harness.\n\tevalScope := evalScopeFromGraphWalk(walker, addrs.RootModuleInstance)\n\n\treturn newState, evalScope, diags\n}\n\nfunc checkApplyTimeVariables(needed collections.Set[string], gotValues InputValues, config *configs.Config) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\tfor name := range needed.All() {\n\t\tif vv, exists := gotValues[name]; !exists || vv.Value == cty.NilVal || vv.Value.IsNull() {\n\t\t\t// This error message assumes that the only possible reason for\n\t\t\t// an apply-time variable is because the variable is ephemeral,\n\t\t\t// which is true at the time of writing. This error message might\n\t\t\t// need to be generalized if we introduce other reasons for\n\t\t\t// apply-time variables in future.\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\t\"No value for required variable\",\n\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"The ephemeral input variable %q was set during the plan phase, and so must also be set during the apply phase.\", name),\n\t\t\t))\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tfor name := range gotValues {\n\t\tif !needed.Has(name) {\n\t\t\t// We'll treat this a little differently depending on whether\n\t\t\t// the variable is declared as ephemeral or not.\n\t\t\tif vc, ok := config.Module.Variables[name]; ok && vc.Ephemeral {\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\t\t\"No value for required variable\",\n\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"The ephemeral input variable %q was not set during the plan phase, and so must remain unset during the apply phase.\", name),\n\t\t\t\t))\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\t\t\"Unexpected new value for variable\",\n\t\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Input variable %q is non-ephemeral, so its value was fixed during planning and cannot be reset during apply.\", name),\n\t\t\t\t))\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn diags\n}\n\nfunc (c *Context) applyGraph(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts, validate bool) (*Graph, walkOperation, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tvariables := InputValues{}\n\tfor name, dyVal := range plan.VariableValues {\n\t\tval, err := dyVal.Decode(cty.DynamicPseudoType)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\n\t\t\t\ttfdiags.Error,\n\t\t\t\t\"Invalid variable value in plan\",\n\t\t\t\tfmt.Sprintf(\"Invalid value for variable %q recorded in plan file: %s.\", name, err),\n\t\t\t))\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\tif pvm, ok := plan.VariableMarks[name]; ok {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\tvariables[name] = &InputValue{\n\t\t\tValue:      cty.NilVal,\n\t\t\tSourceType: ValueFromPlan,\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\toperation := walkApply\n\tif plan.UIMode == plans.DestroyMode {\n\t\t// FIXME: Due to differences in how objects must be handled in the\n\t\t// graph and evaluated during a complete destroy, we must continue to\n\t\t// use plans.DestroyMode to switch on this behavior. cty.Value\n    31→\tif cfg.Default != cty.NilVal {\n    32→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s has a default value\", addr)\n    33→\t\tvar err error\n    34→\t\tdefaultVal, err = convert.Convert(cfg.Default, convertTy)\n    35→\t\tif err != nil {\n    36→\t\t\t// Validation of the declaration should typically catch this,\n    37→\t\t\t// but we'll check it here too to be robust.\n    38→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n    39→\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n    40→\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid default value for module argument\",\n    41→\t\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n    42→\t\t\t\t\t\"The default value for variable %q is incompatible with its type constraint: %s.\",\n    43→\t\t\t\t\tcfg.Name, err,\n    44→\t\t\t\t),\n    45→\t\t\t\tSubject: &cfg.DeclRange,\n    46→\t\t\t})\n    47→\t\t\t// We'll return a placeholder unknown value to avoid producing\n    48→\t\t\t// redundant downstream errors.\n    49→\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cfg.Type), diags\n    50→\t\t}\n    51→\t}\n    52→\n    53→\tvar sourceRange tfdiags.SourceRange\n    54→\tvar nonFileSource string\n    55→\tif raw.HasSourceRange() {\n    56→\t\tsourceRange = raw.SourceRange\n    57→\t} else {\n    58→\t\t// If the value came from a place that isn't a file and thus doesn't\n    59→\t\t// have its own source range, we'll use the declaration range as\n    60→\t\t// our source range and generate some slightly different error\n    61→\t\t// messages.\n    62→\t\tsourceRange = tfdiags.SourceRangeFromHCL(cfg.DeclRange)\n    63→\t\tswitch raw.SourceType {\n    64→\t\tcase ValueFromCLIArg:\n    65→\t\t\tnonFileSource = fmt.Sprintf(\"set using -var=\\\"%s=...\\\"\", addr.Variable.Name)\n    66→\t\tcase ValueFromEnvVar:\n    67→\t\t\tnonFileSource = fmt.Sprintf(\"set using the TF_VAR_%s environment variable\", addr.Variable.Name)\n    68→\t\tcase ValueFromInput:\n    69→\t\t\tnonFileSource = \"set using an interactive prompt\"\n    70→\t\tdefault:\n    71→\t\t\tnonFileSource = \"set from outside of the configuration\"\n    72→\t\t}\n    73→\t}\n    74→\n    75→\tgiven := raw.Value\n    76→\tif given == cty.NilVal { // The variable wasn't set at all (even to null)\n    77→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s has no defined value\", addr)\n    78→\t\tif cfg.Required() {\n    79→\t\t\t// NOTE: The CLI layer typically checks for itself whether all of\n    80→\t\t\t// the required _root_ module variables are set, which would\n    81→\t\t\t// mask this error with a more specific one that refers to the\n    82→\t\t\t// CLI features for setting such variables. We can get here for\n    83→\t\t\t// child module variables, though.\n    84→\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s is required but is not set\", addr)\n    85→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n    86→\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n    87→\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Required variable not set`,\n    88→\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The variable %q is required, but is not set.`, addr.Variable.Name),\n    89→\t\t\t\tSubject:  cfg.DeclRange.Ptr(),\n    90→\t\t\t})\n    91→\t\t\t// We'll return a placeholder unknown value to avoid producing\n    92→\t\t\t// redundant downstream errors.\n    93→\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cfg.Type), diags\n    94→\t\t}\n    95→\n    96→\t\tgiven = defaultVal // must be set, because we checked above that the variable isn't required\n    97→\t}\n    98→\n    99→\t// Apply defaults from the variable's type constraint to the converted value,\n   100→\t// unless the converted value is null. We do not apply defaults to top-level\n   101→\t// null values, as doing so could prevent assigning null to a nullable\n   102→\t// variable.\n   103→\tif cfg.TypeDefaults != nil && !given.IsNull() {\n   104→\t\tgiven = cfg.TypeDefaults.Apply(given)\n   105→\t}\n   106→\n   107→\tval, err := convert.Convert(given, convertTy)\n   108→\tif err != nil {\n   109→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s has unsuitable type\\n  got:  %s\\n  want: %s\", addr, given.Type(), convertTy)\n   110→\t\tvar detail string\n   111→\t\tvar subject *hcl.Range\n   112→\t\tif nonFileSource != \"\" {\n   113→\t\t\tdetail = fmt.Sprintf(\n   114→\t\t\t\t\"Unsuitable value for %s %s: %s.\",\n   115→\t\t\t\taddr, nonFileSource, err,\n   116→\t\t\t)\n   117→\t\t\tsubject = cfg.DeclRange.Ptr()\n   118→\t\t} else {\n   119→\t\t\tdetail = fmt.Sprintf(\n   120→\t\t\t\t\"The given value is not suitable for %s declared at %s: %s.\",\n   121→\t\t\t\taddr, cfg.DeclRange.String(), err,\n   122→\t\t\t)\n   123→\t\t\tsubject = sourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr()\n   124→\n   125→\t\t\t// In some workflows, the operator running terraform does not have access to the variables\n   126→\t\t\t// themselves. They are for example stored in encrypted files that will be used by the CI toolset\n   127→\t\t\t// and not by the operator directly. In such a case, the failing secret value should not be\n   128→\t\t\t// displayed to the operator\n   129→\t\t\tif cfg.Sensitive {\n   130→\t\t\t\tdetail = fmt.Sprintf(\n   131→\t\t\t\t\t\"The given value is not suitable for %s, which is sensitive: %s. Invalid value defined at %s.\",\n   132→\t\t\t\t\taddr, err, sourceRange.ToHCL(),\n   133→\t\t\t\t)\n   134→\t\t\t\tsubject = cfg.DeclRange.Ptr()\n   135→\t\t\t}\n   136→\t\t}\n   137→\n   138→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   139→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   140→\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid value for input variable\",\n   141→\t\t\tDetail:   detail,\n   142→\t\t\tSubject:  subject,\n   143→\t\t})\n   144→\t\t// We'll return a placeholder unknown value to avoid producing\n   145→\t\t// redundant downstream errors.\n   146→\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cfg.Type), diags\n   147→\t}\n   148→\n   149→\t// By the time we get here, we know:\n   150→\t// - val matches the variable's type constraint\n   151→\t// - val is definitely not cty.NilVal, but might be a null value if the given was already null.\n   152→\t//\n   153→\t// That means we just need to handle the case where the value is null,\n   154→\t// which might mean we need to use the default value, or produce an error.\n   155→\t//\n   156→\t// For historical reasons we do this only for a \"non-nullable\" variable.\n   157→\t// Nullable variables just appear as null if they were set to null,\n   158→\t// regardless of any default value.\n   159→\tif val.IsNull() && !cfg.Nullable {\n   160→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s is defined as null\", addr)\n   161→\t\tif defaultVal != cty.NilVal {\n   162→\t\t\tval = defaultVal\n   163→\t\t} else {\n   164→\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s is non-nullable but set to null, and is required\", addr)\n   165→\t\t\tif nonFileSource != \"\" {\n   166→\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   167→\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   168→\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Required variable not set`,\n   169→\t\t\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n   170→\t\t\t\t\t\t\"Unsuitable value for %s %s: required variable may not be set to null.\",\n   171→\t\t\t\t\t\taddr, nonFileSource,\n   172→\t\t\t\t\t),\n   173→\t\t\t\t\tSubject: cfg.DeclRange.Ptr(),\n   174→\t\t\t\t})\n   175→\t\t\t} else {\n   176→\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   177→\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   178→\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Required variable not set`,\n   179→\t\t\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n   180→\t\t\t\t\t\t\"The given value is not suitable for %s defined at %s: required variable may not be set to null.\",\n   181→\t\t\t\t\t\taddr, cfg.DeclRange.String(),\n   182→\t\t\t\t\t),\n   183→\t\t\t\t\tSubject: sourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   184→\t\t\t\t})\n   185→\t\t\t}\n   186→\t\t\t// Stub out our return value so that the semantic checker doesn't\n   187→\t\t\t// produce redundant downstream errors.\n   188→\t\t\tval = cty.UnknownVal(cfg.Type)\n   189→\t\t}\n   190→\t}\n   191→\n   192→\tif !cfg.Ephemeral {\n   193→\t\t// An ephemeral input variable always has an ephemeral value inside the\n   194→\t\t// module, even if the value assigned to it from outside is not. This\n   195→\t\t// is a useful simplification so that module authors can be explicit\n   196→\t\t// about what guarantees they are intending to make (regardless of\n   197→\t\t// current implementation details). Changing the ephemerality of an\n   198→\t\t// input variable is a breaking change to a module's API.\n   199→\t\tval = val.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n   200→\t} else {\n   201→\t\tif marks.Contains(val, marks.Ephemeral) {\n   202→\t\t\tvar subject hcl.Range\n   203→\t\t\tif raw.HasSourceRange() {\n   204→\t\t\t\tsubject = raw.SourceRange.ToHCL()\n   205→\t\t\t} else {\n   206→\t\t\t\t// We shouldn't typically get here for ephemeral values, because\n   207→\t\t\t\t// all of the source types that can represent expressions that\n   208→\t\t\t\t// could potentially produce ephemeral values are those which\n   209→\t\t\t\t// have source locations. This is just here for robustness.\n   210→\t\t\t\tsubject = cfg.DeclRange\n   211→\t\t\t}\n   212→\n   213→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   214→\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   215→\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Ephemeral value not allowed\",\n   216→\t\t\t\tDetail:   \"This input variable is not declared as accepting a ephemeral values, so it cannot be set to a result derived from an ephemeral value.\",\n   217→\t\t\t\tSubject:  subject.Ptr(),\n   218→\t\t\t})\n   219→\t\t}\n   220→\t}\n   221→\n   222→\treturn val, diags\n   223→}\n   224→\n   225→// evalVariableValidations ensures that all of the configured custom validations\n   226→// for a variable are passing.\n   227→//\n   228→// This must be used only after any side-effects that make the value of the\n   229→// variable available for use in expression evaluation, such as\n   230→// EvalModuleCallArgument for variables in descendant modules.\n   231→func evalVariableValidations(addr addrs.AbsInputVariableInstance, ctx EvalContext, rules []*configs.CheckRule, valueRng hcl.Range, validateWalk bool) (diags tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   232→\tif len(rules) == 0 {\n   233→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: no validation rules declared for %s, so skipping\", addr)\n   234→\t\treturn nil\n   235→\t}\n   236→\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: validating %s\", addr)\n   237→\n   238→\tcheckState := ctx.Checks()\n   239→\tif !checkState.ConfigHasChecks(addr.ConfigCheckable()) {\n   240→\t\t// We have nothing to do if this object doesn't have any checks,\n   241→\t\t// but the \"rules\" slice should agree that we don't.\n   242→\t\tif ct := len(rules); ct != 0 {\n   243→\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"check state says that %s should have no rules, but it has %d\", addr, ct))\n   244→\t\t}\n   245→\t\treturn diags\n   246→\t}\n   247→\n   248→\t// We'll build just one evaluation context covering the data needed by\n   249→\t// all of the rules together, since that'll minimize lock contention\n   250→\t// on the state, plan, etc.\n   251→\tscope := ctx.EvaluationScope(nil, nil, EvalDataForNoInstanceKey)\n   252→\tvar refs []*addrs.Reference\n   253→\tfor _, rule := range rules {\n   254→\t\tcondRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.Condition)\n   255→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   256→\t\tmsgRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.ErrorMessage)\n   257→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   258→\t\trefs = append(refs, condRefs...)\n   259→\t\trefs = append(refs, msgRefs...)\n   260→\t}\n   261→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   262→\t\t// If any of the references were invalid then evaluating the expressions\n   263→\t\t// will duplicate those errors, so we'll bail out early.\n   264→\t\treturn diags\n   265→\t}\n   266→\thclCtx, moreDiags := scope.EvalContext(refs)\n   267→\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   268→\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n   269→\t\treturn diags\n   270→\t}\n   271→\n   272→\t// HACK: Historically we manually built a very constrained hcl.EvalContext\n   273→\t// here, which only included the value of the one specific input variable\n   274→\t// we're validating, since we didn't yet support referring to anything\n   275→\t// else. That accidentally bypassed our rule that input variables are\n   276→\t// always unknown during the validate walk, and thus accidentally created\n   277→\t// a useful behavior of actually checking constant-only values against\n   278→\t// their validation rules just during \"terraform validate\", rather than\n   279→\t// having to run \"terraform plan\".\n   280→\t//\n   281→\t// Although that behavior was accidental, it makes simple validation rules\n   282→\t// more useful and is protected by compatibility promises, and so we'll\n   283→\t// fake it here by overwriting the unknown value that scope.EvalContext\n   284→\t// will have inserted with a possibly-more-known value using the same\n   285→\t// strategy our special code used to use.\n   286→\tourVal := ctx.NamedValues().GetInputVariableValue(addr)\n   287→\tif ourVal != cty.NilVal {\n   288→\t\t// (it would be weird for ourVal to be nil here, but we'll tolerate it\n   289→\t\t// because it was scope.EvalContext's responsibility to check for the\n   290→\t\t// absent final value, and even if it didn't we'll just get an\n   291→\t\t// evaluation error when evaluating the expressions below anyway.)\n   292→\n   293→\t\t// Our goal here is to make sure that a reference to the variable\n   294→\t\t// we're checking will evaluate to ourVal, regardless of what else\n   295→\t\t// scope.EvalContext might have put in the variables table.\n   296→\t\tif hclCtx.Variables == nil {\n   297→\t\t\thclCtx.Variables = make(map[string]cty.Value)\n   298→\t\t}\n   299→\t\tif varsVal, ok := hclCtx.Variables[\"var\"]; ok {\n   300→\t\t\t// Unfortunately we need to unpack and repack the object here,\n   301→\t\t\t// because cty values are immutable.\n   302→\t\t\tattrs := varsVal.AsValueMap()\n   303→\t\t\tattrs[addr.Variable.Name] = ourVal\n   304→\t\t\thclCtx.Variables[\"var\"] = cty.ObjectVal(attrs)\n   305→\t\t} else {\n   306→\t\t\thclCtx.Variables[\"var\"] = cty.ObjectVal(map[string]cty.Value{\n   307→\t\t\t\taddr.Variable.Name: ourVal,\n   308→\t\t\t})\n   309→\t\t}\n   310→\t}\n   311→\n   312→\tfor ix, validation := range rules {\n   313→\t\tresult, ruleDiags := evalVariableValidation(validation, hclCtx, valueRng, addr, ix, validateWalk)\n   314→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(ruleDiags)\n   315→\n   316→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s status is now %s\", addr, result.Status)\n   317→\t\tif result.Status == checks.StatusFail {\n   318→\t\t\tcheckState.ReportCheckFailure(addr, addrs.InputValidation, ix, result.FailureMessage)\n   319→\t\t} else {\n   320→\t\t\tcheckState.ReportCheckResult(addr, addrs.InputValidation, ix, result.Status)\n   321→\t\t}\n   322→\t}\n   323→\n   324→\treturn diags\n   325→}\n   326→\n   327→func evalVariableValidation(validation *configs.CheckRule, hclCtx *hcl.EvalContext, valueRng hcl.Range, addr addrs.AbsInputVariableInstance, ix int, validateWalk bool) (checkResult, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   328→\tconst errInvalidCondition = \"Invalid variable validation result\"\n   329→\tconst errInvalidValue = \"Invalid value for variable\"\n   330→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   331→\n   332→\tresult, moreDiags := validation.Condition.Value(hclCtx)\n   333→\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   334→\terrorValue, errorDiags := validation.ErrorMessage.Value(hclCtx)\n   335→\n   336→\t// The following error handling is a workaround to preserve backwards\n   337→\t// compatibility. Due to an implementation quirk, all prior versions of\n   338→\t// Terraform would treat error messages specified using JSON\n   339→\t// configuration syntax (.tf.json) as string literals, even if they\n   340→\t// contained the \"${\" template expression operator. This behaviour did\n   341→\t// not match that of HCL configuration syntax, where a template\n   342→\t// expression would result in a validation error.\n   343→\t//\n   344→\t// As a result, users writing or generating JSON configuration syntax\n   345→\t// may have specified error messages which are invalid template\n   346→\t// expressions. As we add support for error message expressions, we are\n   347→\t// unable to perfectly distinguish between these two cases.\n   348→\t//\n   349→\t// To ensure that we don't break backwards compatibility, we have the\n   350→\t// below fallback logic if the error message fails to evaluate. This\n   351→\t// should only have any effect for JSON configurations. The gohcl\n   352→\t// DecodeExpression function behaves differently when the source of the\n   353→\t// expression is a JSON configuration file and a nil context is passed.\n   354→\tif errorDiags.HasErrors() {\n   355→\t\t// Attempt to decode the expression as a string literal. Passing\n   356→\t\t// nil as the context forces a JSON syntax string value to be\n   357→\t\t// interpreted as a string literal.\n   358→\t\tvar errorString string\n   359→\t\tmoreErrorDiags := gohcl.DecodeExpression(validation.ErrorMessage, nil, &errorString)\n   360→\t\tif !moreErrorDiags.HasErrors() {\n   361→\t\t\t// Decoding succeeded, meaning that this is a JSON syntax\n   362→\t\t\t// string value. We rewrap that as a cty value to allow later\n   363→\t\t\t// decoding to succeed.\n   364→\t\t\terrorValue = cty.StringVal(errorString)\n   365→\n   366→\t\t\t// This warning diagnostic explains this odd behaviour, while\n   367→\t\t\t// giving us an escape hatch to change this to a hard failure\n   368→\t\t\t// in some future Terraform 1.x version.\n   369→\t\t\terrorDiags = hcl.Diagnostics{\n   370→\t\t\t\t&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   371→\t\t\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagWarning,\n   372→\t\t\t\t\tSummary:     \"Validation error message expression is invalid\",\n   373→\t\t\t\t\tDetail:      fmt.Sprintf(\"The error message provided could not be evaluated as an expression, so Terraform is interpreting it as a string literal.\\n\\nIn future versions of Terraform, this will be considered an error. Please file a GitHub issue if this would break your workflow.\\n\\n%s\", errorDiags.Error()),\n   374→\t\t\t\t\tSubject:     validation.ErrorMessage.Range().Ptr(),\n   375→\t\t\t\t\tContext:     validation.DeclRange.Ptr(),\n   376→\t\t\t\t\tExpression:  validation.ErrorMessage,\n   377→\t\t\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n   378→\t\t\t\t},\n   379→\t\t\t}\n   380→\t\t}\n   381→\n   382→\t\t// We want to either report the original diagnostics if the\n   383→\t\t// fallback failed, or the warning generated above if it succeeded.\n   384→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(errorDiags)\n   385→\t}\n   386→\n   387→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   388→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s rule %s check rule evaluation failed: %s\", addr, validation.DeclRange, diags.Err().Error())\n   389→\t}\n   390→\tif !result.IsKnown() {\n   391→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s rule %s condition value is unknown, so skipping validation for now\", addr, validation.DeclRange)\n   392→\n   393→\t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusUnknown}, diags // We'll wait until we've learned more, then.\n   394→\t}\n   395→\tif result.IsNull() {\n   396→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   397→\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n   398→\t\t\tSummary:     errInvalidCondition,\n   399→\t\t\tDetail:      \"Validation condition expression must return either true or false, not null.\",\n   400→\t\t\tSubject:     validation.Condition.Range().Ptr(),\n   401→\t\t\tExpression:  validation.Condition,\n   402→\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n   403→\t\t})\n   404→\t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusError}, diags\n   405→\t}\n   406→\tvar err error\n   407→\tresult, err = convert.Convert(result, cty.Bool)\n   408→\tif err != nil {\n   409→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   410→\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n   411→\t\t\tSummary:     errInvalidCondition,\n   412→\t\t\tDetail:      fmt.Sprintf(\"Invalid validation condition result value: %s.\", tfdiags.FormatError(err)),\n   413→\t\t\tSubject:     validation.Condition.Range().Ptr(),\n   414→\t\t\tExpression:  validation.Condition,\n   415→\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n   416→\t\t})\n   417→\t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusError}, diags\n   418→\t}\n   419→\n   420→\t// Validation condition may be marked if the input variable is bound to\n   421→\t// a sensitive value. This is irrelevant to the validation process, so\n   422→\t// we discard the marks now.\n   423→\tresult, _ = result.Unmark()\n   424→\tstatus := checks.StatusForCtyValue(result)\n   425→\n   426→\tif status != checks.StatusFail {\n   427→\t\treturn checkResult{Status: status}, diags\n   428→\t}\n   429→\n   430→\tif !errorValue.IsKnown() {\n   431→\t\tif validateWalk {\n   432→\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[DEBUG] evalVariableValidations: %s rule %s error_message value is unknown, so skipping validation for now\", addr, validation.DeclRange)\n   433→\t\t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusUnknown}, diags\n   434→\t\t}\n   435→\n   436→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   437→\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n   438→\t\t\tSummary:     \"Invalid error message\",\n   439→\t\t\tDetail:      \"Unsuitable value for error message: expression refers to values that won't be known until the apply phase.\",\n   440→\t\t\tSubject:     validation.ErrorMessage.Range().Ptr(),\n   441→\t\t\tExpression:  validation.ErrorMessage,\n   442→\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n   443→\t\t\tExtra:       diagnosticCausedByUnknown(true),\n   444→\t\t})\n   445→\t\treturn checkResult{\n   446→\t\t\tStatus: checks.StatusError,\n   447→\t\t}, diags\n   448→\t}\n   449→\n   450→\tvar errorMessage string\n   451→\tif !errorDiags.HasErrors() && !errorValue.IsNull() {\n   452→\t\tvar err error\n   453→\t\terrorValue, err = convert.Convert(errorValue, cty.String)\n   454→\t\tif err != nil {\n   455→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n Terraform will not display the resulting message.\n   484→\n   485→You can correct this by removing references to ephemeral values, or by carefully using the ephemeralasnull() function if the expression will not reveal the ephemeral data.`,\n   486→\n   487→\t\t\t\t\tSubject:     validation.ErrorMessage.Range().Ptr(),\n   488→\t\t\t\t\tExpression:  validation.ErrorMessage,\n   489→\t\t\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n   490→\t\t\t\t})\n   491→\t\t\t\terrorMessage = \"The error message included a sensitive value, so it will not be displayed.\"\n   492→\t\t\t} else {\n   493→\t\t\t\terrorMessage = strings.TrimSpace(errorValue.AsString())\n   494→\t\t\t}\n   495→\t\t}\n   496→\t}\n   497→\tif errorMessage == \"\" {\n   498→\t\terrorMessage = \"Failed to evaluate condition error message.\"\n   499→\t}\n   500→\n   501→\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   502→\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n   503→\t\tSummary:     errInvalidValue,\n   504→\t\tDetail:      fmt.Sprintf(\"%s\\n\\nThis was checked by the validation rule at %s.\", errorMessage, validation.DeclRange.String()),\n   505→\t\tSubject:     valueRng.Ptr(),\n   506→\t\tExpression:  validation.Condition,\n   507→\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n   508→\t\tExtra: &addrs.CheckRuleDiagnosticExtra{\n   509→\t\t\tCheckRule: addr.CheckRule(addrs.InputValidation, ix),\n   510→\t\t},\n   511→\t})\n   512→\n   513→\treturn checkResult{\n   514→\t\tStatus:         status,\n   515→\t\tFailureMessage: errorMessage,\n   516→\t}, diags\n   517→}\n   518→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. prepareFinalInputVariableValue(addr addrs.AbsInputVariableInstance, raw *InputValue, cfg *configs.Variable) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tconvertTy := cfg.ConstraintType\n\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: preparing %s\", addr)\n\n\tvar defaultVal cty.Value\n\tif cfg.Default != cty.NilVal {\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s has a default value\", addr)\n\t\tvar err error\n\t\tdefaultVal, err = convert.Convert(cfg.Default, convertTy)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t// Validation of the default value for module argument\",\n\t\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\t\"The default value for variable %q is incompatible with its type constraint: %s.\",\n\t\t\t\t\tcfg.Name, error\n\t\t// messages.\n\t\tsourceRange = tfdiags.SourceRangeFromHCL(cfg.DeclRange)\n\t\tswitch raw.SourceType {\n\t\tcase ValueFromCLIArg:\n\t\t\tnonFileSource = fmt.Sprintf(\"set using -var=\\\"%s=...\\\"\", addr.Variable.Name)\n\t\tcase ValueFromEnvVar:\n\t\t\tnonFileSource = fmt.Sprintf(\"set using the TF_VAR_%s environment variable\", addr.Variable.Name)\n\t\tcase given == cty.NilVal { // The variable wasn't set at all (even to null)\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s has no defined value\", addr)\n\t\tif cfg.Required() {\n\t\t\t// NOTE: The CLI layer typically checks for itself whether all of\n\t\t\t// the required _root_ module variables are set, which would\n\t\t\t// mask this error with a more specific one that refers to the\n\t\t\t// CLI features for setting such variables. We can get here for\n\t\t\t// child module variables, though.\n\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s is required but is not set\", addr)\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Required variable not set`,\n\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The variable %q is required, but is not set.`, addr.Variable.Name),\n\t\t\t\tSubject:  cfg.DeclRange.Ptr(),\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t// We'll return a placeholder unknown value to avoid producing\n\t\t\t// redundant downstream errors.\n\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cfg.Type), diags\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tgiven = defaultVal // must be set, because we checked above that the variable isn't required\n\t}\n\n\t// Apply defaults from the variable's type constraint to the converted value,\n\t// unless the converted value is null. We do not apply defaults to top-level\n\t// null values, as doing so could prevent assigning null to a nullable\n\t// variable.\n\tif cfg.TypeDefaults != nil && !given.IsNull() {\n\t\tgiven = cfg.TypeDefaults.Apply(given)\n\t}\n\n\tval, err := convert.Convert(given, convertTy)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s has unsuitable type\\n  got:  %s\\n  want: %s\", addr, given.Type(), convertTy)\n\t\tvar detail string\n\t\tvar subject *hcl.Range\n\t\tif nonFileSource != \"\" {\n\t\t\tdetail = fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\"Unsuitable value for %s %s: %s.\",\n\t\t\t\taddr, nonFileSource, err,\n\t\t\t)\n\t\t\tsubject = cfg.DeclRange.Ptr()\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tdetail = fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\"The given value is not suitable for %s declared at %s: %s.\",\n\t\t\t\taddr, cfg.DeclRange.String(), err,\n\t\t\t)\n\t\t\tsubject = sourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr()\n\n\t\t\t// In some workflows, the operator running terraform does not have access to the variables\n\t\t\t// themselves. They are for example stored in encrypted files that will be used by the CI toolset\n\t\t\t// and not by the operator directly. In such a case, the failing secret value should not be\n\t\t\t// displayed to the operator\n\t\t\tif cfg.Sensitive {\n\t\t\t\tdetail = fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\t\"The given value is not suitable for %s, which is sensitive: %s. Invalid value defined at %s.\",\n\t\t\t\t\taddr, err, sourceRange.ToHCL(),\n\t\t\t\t)\n\t\t\t\tsubject = cfg.DeclRange.Ptr()\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid value for input variable\",\n\t\t\tDetail:   detail,\n\t\t\tSubject:  subject,\n\t\t})\n\t\t// We'll return a placeholder unknown value to avoid producing\n\t\t// redundant downstream errors.\n\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cfg.Type), diags\n\t}\n\n\t// By the time we get here, we know:\n\t// - val matches the variable's type constraint\n\t// - val is definitely not cty.NilVal, but might be a null value if the given was already null.\n\t//\n\t// That means we just need to handle the case where the value is null,\n\t// which might mean we need to use the default value, or produce an error.\n\t//\n\t// For historical reasons we do this only for a \"non-nullable\" variable.\n\t// Nullable variables just appear as null if they were set to null,\n\t// regardless of any default value.\n\tif val.IsNull() && !cfg.Nullable {\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s is defined as null\", addr)\n\t\tif defaultVal != cty.NilVal {\n\t\t\tval = defaultVal\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] prepareFinalInputVariableValue: %s is non-nullable but set to null, and is required\", addr)\n\t\t\tif nonFileSource != \"\" {\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Required variable not set`,\n\t\t\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\"Unsuitable value for %s %s: required variable may not be set to null.\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\taddr, nonFileSource,\n\t\t\t\t\t),\n\t\t\t\t\tSubject: cfg.DeclRange.Ptr(),\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Required variable not set`,\n\t\t\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\"The given value is not suitable for %s defined at %s: required variable may not be set to null.\",\n\t\t\t\t\t\taddr, cfg.DeclRange.String(),\n\t\t\t\t\t),\n\t\t\t\t\tSubject: sourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t\t\t})\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t// Stub out our return value so that the semantic checker doesn't\n\t\t\t// produce redundant downstream errors.\n\t\t\tval = cty.UnknownVal(cfg.Type)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tif !cfg.Ephemeral {\n\t\t// An ephemeral input variable always has an ephemeral value inside the\n\t\t// module, even if the value assigned to it from outside is not. This\n\t\t// is a useful simplification so that module authors can be explicit\n\t\t// about what guarantees they are intending to make (regardless of\n\t\t// current implementation details). Changing the ephemerality of an\n\t\t// input variable is a breaking change to a module's API.\n\t\tval = val.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n\t} else {\n\t\tif marks.Contains(val, marks.Ephemeral) {\n\t\t\tvar subject hcl.Range\n\t\t\tif raw.HasSourceRange() {\n\t\t\t\tsubject = raw.SourceRange.ToHCL()\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// We shouldn't typically get here for ephemeral values, because\n\t\t\t\t// all of the source types that can represent expressions that\n\t\t\t\t// could potentially produce ephemeral values are those which\n\t\t\t\t// have source locations. This is just here for robustness.\n\t\t\t\tsubject = cfg.DeclRange\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Ephemeral value not allowed\",\n\t\t\t\tDetail:   \"This input variable is not declared as accepting a ephemeral values, so it cannot be set to a result derived from an ephemeral value.\",\n\t\t\t\tSubject:  subject.Ptr(),\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn val, diags\n}\n\n// evalVariableValidations ensures that all of the configured custom validations\n// for a variable are passing.\n//\n// This must be used only after any side-effects that make the value of the\n// variable available for use in expression evaluation, such as\n// EvalModuleCallArgument for variables in descendant modules.\nfunc evalVariableValidations(addr addrs.AbsInputVariableInstance, ctx EvalContext, rules []*configs.CheckRule, valueRng hcl.Range, validateWalk bool) (diags tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tif len(rules) == 0 {\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: no validation rules declared for %s, so skipping\", addr)\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: validating %s\", addr)\n\n\tcheckState := ctx.Checks()\n\tif !checkState.ConfigHasChecks(addr.ConfigCheckable()) {\n\t\t// We have nothing to do if this object doesn't have any checks,\n\t\t// but the \"rules\" slice should agree that we don't.\n\t\tif ct := len(rules); ct != 0 {\n\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"check state says that %s should have no rules, but it has %d\", addr, ct))\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn diags\n\t}\n\n\t// We'll build just one evaluation context covering the data needed by\n\t// all of the rules together, since that'll minimize lock contention\n\t// on the state, plan, etc.\n\tscope := ctx.EvaluationScope(nil, nil, EvalDataForNoInstanceKey)\n\tvar refs []*addrs.Reference\n\tfor _, rule := range rules {\n\t\tcondRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.Condition)\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\t\tmsgRefs, moreDiags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(addrs.ParseRef, rule.ErrorMessage)\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\t\trefs = append(refs, condRefs...)\n\t\trefs = append(refs, msgRefs...)\n\t}\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// If any of the references were invalid then evaluating the expressions\n\t\t// will duplicate those errors, so we'll bail out early.\n\t\treturn diags\n\t}\n\thclCtx, moreDiags := scope.EvalContext(refs)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\tif moreDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn diags\n\t}\n\n\t// HACK: Historically we manually built a very constrained hcl.EvalContext\n\t// here, which only included the value of the one specific input variable\n\t// we're validating, since we didn't yet support referring to anything\n\t// else. That accidentally bypassed our rule that input variables are\n\t// always unknown during the validate walk, and thus accidentally created\n\t// a useful behavior of actually checking constant-only values against\n\t// their validation rules just during \"terraform validate\", rather than\n\t// having to run \"terraform plan\".\n\t//\n\t// Although that behavior was accidental, it makes simple validation rules\n\t// more useful and is protected by compatibility promises, and so we'll\n\t// fake it here by overwriting the unknown value that scope.EvalContext\n\t// will have inserted with a possibly-more-known value using the same\n\t// strategy our special code used to use.\n\tourVal := ctx.NamedValues().GetInputVariableValue(addr)\n\tif ourVal != cty.NilVal {\n\t\t// (it would be weird for ourVal to be nil here, but we'll tolerate it\n\t\t// because it was scope.EvalContext's responsibility to check for the\n\t\t// absent final value, and even if it didn't we'll just get an\n\t\t// evaluation error when evaluating the expressions below anyway.)\n\n\t\t// Our goal here is to make sure that a reference to the variable\n\t\t// we're checking will evaluate to ourVal, regardless of what else\n\t\t// scope.EvalContext might have put in the variables table.\n\t\tif hclCtx.Variables == nil {\n\t\t\thclCtx.Variables = make(map[string]cty.Value)\n\t\t}\n\t\tif varsVal, ok := hclCtx.Variables[\"var\"]; ok {\n\t\t\t// Unfortunately we need to unpack and repack the object here,\n\t\t\t// because cty values are immutable.\n\t\t\tattrs := varsVal.AsValueMap()\n\t\t\tattrs[addr.Variable.Name] = ourVal\n\t\t\thclCtx.Variables[\"var\"] = cty.ObjectVal(attrs)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\thclCtx.Variables[\"var\"] = cty.ObjectVal(map[string]cty.Value{\n\t\t\t\taddr.Variable.Name: ourVal,\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tfor ix, validation := range rules {\n\t\tresult, ruleDiags := evalVariableValidation(validation, hclCtx, valueRng, addr, ix, validateWalk)\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(ruleDiags)\n\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s status is now %s\", addr, result.Status)\n\t\tif result.Status == checks.StatusFail {\n\t\t\tcheckState.ReportCheckFailure(addr, addrs.InputValidation, ix, result.FailureMessage)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tcheckState.ReportCheckResult(addr, addrs.InputValidation, ix, result.Status)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn diags\n}\n\nfunc evalVariableValidation(validation *configs.CheckRule, hclCtx *hcl.EvalContext, valueRng hcl.Range, addr addrs.AbsInputVariableInstance, ix int, validateWalk bool) (checkResult, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tconst errInvalidCondition = \"Invalid variable validation result\"\n\tconst errInvalidValue = \"Invalid value for variable\"\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tresult, moreDiags := validation.Condition.Value(hclCtx)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\terrorValue, errorDiags := validation.ErrorMessage.Value(hclCtx)\n\n\t// The following error handling is a workaround to preserve backwards\n\t// compatibility. Due to an implementation quirk, all prior versions of\n\t// Terraform would treat error messages specified using JSON\n\t// configuration syntax (.tf.json) as string literals, even if they\n\t// contained the \"${\" template expression operator. This behaviour did\n\t// not match that of HCL configuration syntax, where a template\n\t// expression would result in a validation error.\n\t//\n\t// As a result, users writing or generating JSON configuration syntax\n\t// may have specified error messages which are invalid template\n\t// expressions. As we add support for error message expressions, we are\n\t// unable to perfectly distinguish between these two cases.\n\t//\n\t// To ensure that we don't break backwards compatibility, we have the\n\t// below fallback logic if the error message fails to evaluate. This\n\t// should only have any effect for JSON configurations. The gohcl\n\t// DecodeExpression function behaves differently when the source of the\n\t// expression is a JSON configuration file and a nil context is passed.\n\tif errorDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// Attempt to decode the expression as a string literal. Passing\n\t\t// nil as the context forces a JSON syntax string value to be\n\t\t// interpreted as a string literal.\n\t\tvar errorString string\n\t\tmoreErrorDiags := gohcl.DecodeExpression(validation.ErrorMessage, nil, &errorString)\n\t\tif !moreErrorDiags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t\t// Decoding succeeded, meaning that this is a JSON syntax\n\t\t\t// string value. We rewrap that as a cty value to allow later\n\t\t\t// decoding to succeed.\n\t\t\terrorValue = cty.StringVal(errorString)\n\n\t\t\t// This warning diagnostic explains this odd behaviour, while\n\t\t\t// giving us an escape hatch to change this to a hard failure\n\t\t\t// in some future Terraform 1.x version.\n\t\t\terrorDiags = hcl.Diagnostics{\n\t\t\t\t&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagWarning,\n\t\t\t\t\tSummary:     \"Validation error message expression is invalid\",\n\t\t\t\t\tDetail:      fmt.Sprintf(\"The error message provided could not be evaluated as an expression, so Terraform is interpreting it as a string literal.\\n\\nIn future versions of Terraform, this will be considered an error. Please file a GitHub issue if this would break your workflow.\\n\\n%s\", errorDiags.Error()),\n\t\t\t\t\tSubject:     validation.ErrorMessage.Range().Ptr(),\n\t\t\t\t\tContext:     validation.DeclRange.Ptr(),\n\t\t\t\t\tExpression:  validation.ErrorMessage,\n\t\t\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n\t\t\t\t},\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// We want to either report the original diagnostics if the\n\t\t// fallback failed, or the warning generated above if it succeeded.\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(errorDiags)\n\t}\n\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s rule %s check rule evaluation failed: %s\", addr, validation.DeclRange, diags.Err().Error())\n\t}\n\tif !result.IsKnown() {\n\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalVariableValidations: %s rule %s condition value is unknown, so skipping validation for now\", addr, validation.DeclRange)\n\n\t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusUnknown}, diags // We'll wait until we've learned more, then.\n\t}\n\tif result.IsNull() {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:     errInvalidCondition,\n\t\t\tDetail:      \"Validation condition expression must return either true or false, not null.\",\n\t\t\tSubject:     validation.Condition.Range().Ptr(),\n\t\t\tExpression:  validation.Condition,\n\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusError}, diags\n\t}\n\tvar err error\n\tresult, err = convert.Convert(result, cty.Bool)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:     errInvalidCondition,\n\t\t\tDetail:      fmt.Sprintf(\"Invalid validation condition result value: %s.\", tfdiags.FormatError(err)),\n\t\t\tSubject:     validation.Condition.Range().Ptr(),\n\t\t\tExpression:  validation.Condition,\n\t\t\tEvalContext: hclCtx,\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn checkResult{Status: checks.StatusError}, diags\n\t}\n\n\t// Validation condition may be marked if the input variable is bound to\n\t// a sensitive value.
