should be caught during static validation.\n   370→\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"output value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n   371→\t}\n   372→\toutputConfigs := moduleConfig.Module.Outputs\n   373→\n   374→\t// We don't do instance expansion during validation, and so we need to\n   375→\t// return an unknown value. Technically we should always return\n   376→\t// cty.DynamicVal here because the final value during plan will always\n   377→\t// be an object or tuple type with unpredictable attributes/elements,\n   378→\t// but because we never actually carry values forward from validation to\n   379→\t// planning we lie a little here and return unknown list and map types,\n   380→\t// just to give us more opportunities to catch author mistakes during\n   381→\t// validation.\n   382→\t//\n   383→\t// This means that in practice any expression that refers to a module\n   384→\t// call must be written to be valid for either a collection type or\n   385→\t// structural type of similar kind, so that it can be considered as\n   386→\t// valid during both the validate and plan walks.\n   387→\tif d.Operation == walkValidate {\n   388→\t\tatys := make(map[string]cty.Type, len(outputConfigs))\n   389→\t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n   390→\t\t\tatys[name] = cty.DynamicPseudoType // output values are dynamically-typed\n   391→\t\t}\n   392→\t\tinstTy := cty.Object(atys)\n   393→\n   394→\t\tswitch {\n   395→\t\tcase callConfig.Count != nil:\n   396→\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.List(instTy)), diags\n   397→\t\tcase callConfig.ForEach != nil:\n   398→\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.Map(instTy)), diags\n   399→\t\tdefault:\n   400→\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(instTy), diags\n   401→\t\t}\n   402→\t}\n   403→\n   404→\t// For all other walk types, we proceed to dynamic evaluation of individual\n   405→\t// instances, using the global instance expander. An earlier graph node\n   406→\t// should always have registered the expansion of this module call before\n   407→\t// we get here, unless there's a bug in the graph builders.\n   408→\tallInstances := d.Evaluator.Instances\n   409→\tinstKeyType, instKeys, known := allInstances.ExpandAbsModuleCall(absAddr)\n   410→\tif !known {\n   411→\t\t// If we don't know which instances exist then we can't really predict\n   412→\t\t// anything at all. We can't even predict the return type based on\n   413→\t\t// instKeyType because output values are dynamically-typed and so\n   414→\t\t// our final result will always be an object or tuple type whose\n   415→\t\t// attribute/element count we cannot predict.\n   416→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   417→\t}\n   418→\n   419→\tinstanceObjVal := func(instKey addrs.InstanceKey) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   420→\t\t// This function must always return a valid value, even if it's\n   421→\t\t// just a cty.DynamicVal placeholder accompanying error diagnostics.\n   422→\t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   423→\n   424→\t\tnamedVals := d.Evaluator.NamedValues\n   425→\t\tmoduleInstAddr := absAddr.Instance(instKey)\n   426→\t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(outputConfigs))\n   427→\t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n   428→\t\t\toutputAddr := moduleInstAddr.OutputValue(name)\n   429→\n   430→\t\t\t// Although we do typically expect the graph dependencies to\n   431→\t\t\t// ensure that values get registered before they are needed,\n   432→\t\t\t// we track depedencies with specific output values where\n   433→\t\t\t// possible, instead of with entire module calls, and so\n   434→\t\t\t// in this specific case it's valid for some of this call's\n   435→\t\t\t// output values to not be known yet, with the graph builder\n   436→\t\t\t// being responsible for making sure that no expression\n   437→\t\t\t// in the configuration can actually observe that.\n   438→\t\t\tif !namedVals.HasOutputValue(outputAddr) {\n   439→\t\t\t\tattrs[name] = cty.DynamicVal\n   440→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   441→\t\t\t}\n   442→\t\t\toutputVal := namedVals.GetOutputValue(outputAddr)\n   443→\t\t\tattrs[name] = outputVal\n   444→\t\t}\n   445→\n   446→\t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n   447→\t}\n   448→\n   449→\tswitch instKeyType {\n   450→\n   451→\tcase addrs.NoKeyType:\n   452→\t\t// In this case we should always have exactly one instance that\n   453→\t\t// is addrs.NoKey. If not then there's a bug in the [instances.Expander]\n   454→\t\t// implementation.\n   455→\t\tif len(instKeys) != 1 {\n   456→\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"module call has no instance key type but has %d instances (should be 1)\", len(instKeys)))\n   457→\t\t}\n   458→\t\tret, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKeys[0])\n   459→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   460→\t\treturn ret, diags\n   461→\n   462→\tcase addrs.IntKeyType:\n   463→\t\t// We can assume that the instance keys are in ascending numerical order\n   464→\t\t// and are consecutive, per the contract of allInstances.ExpandModuleCall.\n   465→\t\telems := make([]cty.Value, 0, len(instKeys))\n   466→\t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n   467→\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n   468→\t\t\telems = append(elems, instVal)\n   469→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   470→\t\t}\n   471→\t\treturn cty.TupleVal(elems), diags\n   472→\n   473→\tcase addrs.StringKeyType:\n   474→\t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(instKeys))\n   475→\t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n   476→\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n   477→\t\t\tattrs[string(instKey.(addrs.StringKey))] = instVal\n   478→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n   479→\t\t}\n   480→\t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n   481→\n   482→\tdefault:\n   483→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   484→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   485→\t\t\tSummary:  `Unsupported instance key type`,\n   486→\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n   487→\t\t\t\t`Module call %s has instance key type %#v, which is not supported by the expression evaluator. This is a bug in Terraform.`,\n   488→\t\t\t\tabsAddr, instKeyType,\n   489→\t\t\t),\n   490→\t\t\tSubject: rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   491→\t\t})\n   492→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   493→\t}\n   494→}\n   495→\n   496→func (d *evaluationStateData) GetResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   497→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   498→\t// First we'll consult the configuration to see if an resource of this\n   499→\t// name is declared at all.\n   500→\tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath\n   501→\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendantForInstance(moduleAddr)\n   502→\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n   503→\t\t// should never happen, since we can't be evaluating in a module\n   504→\t\t// that wasn't mentioned in configuration.\n   505→\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"resource value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n   506→\t}\n   507→\n   508→\tconfig := moduleConfig.Module.ResourceByAddr(addr)\n   509→\tif config == nil {\n   510→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   511→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   512→\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared resource`,\n   513→\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`A resource %q %q has not been declared in %s`, addr.Type, addr.Name, moduleDisplayAddr(moduleAddr)),\n   514→\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   515→\t\t})\n   516→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   517→\t}\n   518→\n   519→\t// Much of this function was written before we had factored out the handling\n   520→\t// of instance keys into the separate instance expander model, and so it\n   521→\t// does a bunch of instance-related work itself below.\n   522→\t//\n   523→\t// Currently, unknown instance keys are only possible when planning with\n   524→\t// DeferralAllowed set to true in the PlanOpts, which should only be the\n   525→\t// case in the stacks runtime (not the \"normal terraform\" modules runtime).\n   526→\t// Thus, we have some amount of duplicated code remaining, to be more\n   527→\t// certain that stacks-specific behaviors won't leak out into the standard\n   528→\t// runtime.\n   529→\t//\n   530→\t// TODO: When deferred actions are more stable and robust in stacks, it\n   531→\t// would be nice to rework this function to rely on the ResourceInstanceKeys\n   532→\t// result for _all_ of its work, rather than continuing to duplicate a bunch\n   533→\t// of the logic we've tried to encapsulate over ther already.\n   534→\tif d.Operation == walkPlan || d.Operation == walkApply {\n   535→\t\tif _, _, hasUnknownKeys := d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys(addr.Absolute(moduleAddr)); !hasUnknownKeys {\n   536→\t\t\t// There really isn't anything interesting we can do in this situation,\n   537→\t\t\t// because it means we have an unknown for_each/count, in which case\n   538→\t\t\t// we can't even predict what the result type will be because it\n   539→\t\t\t// would be either an object or tuple type decided based on the instance\n   540→\t\t\t// keys.\n   541→\t\t\t// (We can't get in here for a single-instance resource because in that\n   542→\t\t\t// case we would know that there's only one key and it's addrs.NoKey,\n   543→\t\t\t// so we'll fall through to the other logic below.)\n   544→\t\t\tunknownVal := cty.DynamicVal\n   545→\n   546→\t\t\t// If an ephemeral resource is deferred we need to mark the returned unknown value as ephemeral\n   547→\t\t\tif addr.Mode == addrs.EphemeralResourceMode {\n   548→\t\t\t\tunknownVal = unknownVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n   549→\t\t\t}\n   550→\t\t\treturn unknownVal, diags\n   551→\t\t}\n   552→\t}\n   553→\n   554→\t// Build the provider address from configuration, since we may not have\n   555→\t// state available in all cases.\n   556→\t// We need to build an abs provider address, but we can use a default\n   557→\t// instance since we're only interested in the schema.\n   558→\tschema := d.getResourceSchema(addr, config.Provider)\n   559→\tif schema == nil {\n   560→\t\t// This shouldn't happen, since validation before we get here should've\n   561→\t\t// taken care of it, but we'll show a reasonable error message anyway.\n   562→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   563→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   564→\t\t\tSummary:  `Missing resource type schema`,\n   565→\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"No schema is available for %s in %s. This is a bug in Terraform and should be reported.\", addr, config.Provider),\n   566→\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   567→\t\t})\n   568→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   569→\t}\n   570→\tty := schema.ImpliedType()\n   571→\n   572→\tif addr.Mode == addrs.EphemeralResourceMode {\n   573→\t\t// FIXME: This does not yet work with deferrals, and it would be nice to\n   574→\t\t// find some way to refactor this so that the following code is not so\n   575→\t\t// tethered to the current implementation details. Instead we should\n   576→\t\t// have an abstract idea of first determining what instances the\n   577→\t\t// resource has (using d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys) and\n   578→\t\t// then retrieving the value for each instance to assemble into the\n   579→\t\t// result, using some per-resource-mode logic maintained elsewhere.\n   580→\t\treturn d.getEphemeralResource(addr, rng)\n   581→\t}\n   582→\n   583→\trs := d.Evaluator.State.Resource(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath))\n   584→\n   585→\tif rs == nil {\n   586→\t\tswitch d.Operation {\n   587→\t\tcase walkPlan, walkApply:\n   588→\t\t\t// During plan and apply as we evaluate each removed instance they\n   589→\t\t\t// are removed from the working state. Since we know there are no\n   590→\t\t\t// instances, return an empty container of the expected type.\n   591→\t\t\tswitch {\n   592→\t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n   593→\t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyTupleVal, diags\n   594→\t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n   595→\t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyObjectVal, diags\n   596→\t\t\tdefault:\n   597→\t\t\t\t// While we can reference an expanded resource with 0\n   598→\t\t\t\t// instances, we cannot reference instances that do not exist.\n   599→\t\t\t\t// Due to the fact that we may have direct references to\n   600→\t\t\t\t// instances that may end up in a root output during destroy\n   601→\t\t\t\t// (since a planned destroy cannot yet remove root outputs), we\n   602→\t\t\t\t// need to return a dynamic value here to allow evaluation to\n   603→\t\t\t\t// continue.\n   604→\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] unknown instance %q referenced during %s\", addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath), d.Operation)\n   605→\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   606→\t\t\t}\n   607→\n   608→\t\tcase walkImport:\n   609→\t\t\t// Import does not yet plan resource changes, so new resources from\n   610→\t\t\t// config are not going to be found here. Once walkImport fully\n   611→\t\t\t// plans resources, this case should not longer be needed.\n   612→\t\t\t// In the single instance case, we can return a typed unknown value\n   613→\t\t\t// for the instance to better satisfy other expressions using the\n   614→\t\t\t// value. This of course will not help if statically known\n   615→\t\t\t// attributes are expected to be known elsewhere, but reduces the\n   616→\t\t\t// number of problematic configs for now.\n   617→\t\t\t// Unlike in plan and apply above we can't be sure the count or\n   618→\t\t\t// for_each instances are empty, so we return a DynamicVal. We\n   619→\t\t\t// don't really have a good value to return otherwise -- empty\n   620→\t\t\t// values will fail for direct index expressions, and unknown\n   621→\t\t\t// Lists and Maps could fail in some type unifications.\n   622→\t\t\tswitch {\n   623→\t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n   624→\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   625→\t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n   626→\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   627→\t\t\tdefault:\n   628→\t\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(ty), diags\n   629→\t\t\t}\n   630→\n   631→\t\tdefault:\n   632→\t\t\t// We should only end up here during the validate walk (or\n   633→\t\t\t// console/eval), since later walks should have at least partial\n   634→\t\t\t// states populated for all resources in the configuration.\n   635→\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n   636→\t\t}\n   637→\t}\n   638→\n   639→\t// Now, we're going to build up a value that represents the resource\n   640→\t// or resources that are in the state.\n   641→\tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\n   642→\n   643→\t// First, we're going to load any instances that we have written into the\n   644→\t// deferrals system. A deferred resource overrides anything that might be\n   645→\t// in the state for the resource, so we do this first.\n   646→\tfor key, value := range d.Evaluator.Deferrals.GetDeferredResourceInstances(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)) {\n   647→\t\tinstances[key] = value\n   648→\t}\n   649→\n   650→\t// Decode all instances in the current state\n   651→\tpendingDestroy := d.Operation == walkDestroy\n   652→\tfor key, is := range rs.Instances {\n   653→\t\tif _, ok := instances[key]; ok {\n   654→\t\t\t// Then we've already loaded this instance from the deferrals so\n   655→\t\t\t// we'll just ignore it being in state.\n   656→\t\t\tcontinue\n   657→\t\t}\n   658→\t\t// Otherwise, we'll load the instance from state.\n   659→\n   660→\t\tif is == nil || is.Current == nil {\n   661→\t\t\t// Assume we're dealing with an instance that hasn't been created yet.\n   662→\t\t\tinstances[key] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n   663→\t\t\tcontinue\n   664→\t\t}\n   665→\n   666→\t\tinstAddr := addr.Instance(key).Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n   667→\t\tchange := d.Evaluator.Changes.GetResourceInstanceChange(instAddr, addrs.NotDeposed)\n   668→\t\tif change != nil {\n   669→\t\t\t// Don't take any resources that are yet to be deleted into account.\n   670→\t\t\t// If the referenced resource is CreateBeforeDestroy, then orphaned\n   671→\t\t\t// instances will be in the state, as they are not destroyed until\n   672→\t\t\t// after their dependants are updated.\n   673→\t\t\tif change.Action == plans.Delete {\n   674→\t\t\t\tif !pendingDestroy {\n   675→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   676→\t\t\t\t}\n   677→\t\t\t}\n   678→\t\t}\n   679→\n   680→\t\t// Planned resources are temporarily stored in state with empty values,\n   681→\t\t// and need to be replaced by the planned value here.\n   682→\t\tif is.Current.Status == states.ObjectPlanned {\n   683→\t\t\tif change == nil {\n   684→\t\t\t\t// FIXME: This is usually an unfortunate case where we need to\n   685→\t\t\t\t// lookup an individual instance referenced via \"self\" for\n   686→\t\t\t\t// postconditions which we know exists, but because evaluation\n   687→\t\t\t\t// must always get the resource in aggregate some instance\n   688→\t\t\t\t// changes may not yet be registered.\n   689→\t\t\t\tinstances[key] = cty.DynamicVal\n   690→\t\t\t\t// log the problem for debugging, since it may be a legitimate error we can't catch\n   691→\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[WARN] instance %s is marked as having a change pending but that change is not recorded in the plan\", instAddr)\n   692→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   693→\t\t\t}\n   694→\t\t\tinstances[key] = change.After\n   695→\t\t\tcontinue\n   696→\t\t}\n   697→\n   698→\t\tios, err := is.Current.Decode(ty)\n   699→\t\tif err != nil {\n   700→\t\t\t// This shouldn't happen, since by the time we get here we\n   701→\t\t\t// should have upgraded the state data already.\n   702→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   703→\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   704→\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid resource instance data in state\",\n   705→\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Instance %s data could not be decoded from the state: %s.\", instAddr, err),\n   706→\t\t\t\tSubject:  &config.DeclRange,\n   707→\t\t\t})\n   708→\t\t\tcontinue\n   709→\t\t}\n   710→\n   711→\t\tval := ios.Value\n   712→\n   713→\t\tinstances[key] = val\n   714→\t}\n   715→\n   716→\t// ret should be populated with a valid value in all cases below\n   717→\tvar ret cty.Value\n   718→\n   719→\tswitch {\n   720→\tcase config.Count != nil:\n   721→\t\t// figure out what the last index we have is\n   722→\t\tlength := -1\n   723→\t\tfor key := range instances {\n   724→\t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n   725→\t\t\tif !ok {\n   726→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   727→\t\t\t}\n   728→\t\t\tif int(intKey) >= length {\n   729→\t\t\t\tlength = int(intKey) + 1\n   730→\t\t\t}\n   731→\t\t}\n   732→\n   733→\t\tif length > 0 {\n   734→\t\t\tvals := make([]cty.Value, length)\n   735→\t\t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n   736→\t\t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n   737→\t\t\t\tif !ok {\n   738→\t\t\t\t\t// old key from state, which isn't valid for evaluation\n   739→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   740→\t\t\t\t}\n   741→\n   742→\t\t\t\tvals[int(intKey)] = instance\n   743→\t\t\t}\n   744→\n   745→\t\t\t// Insert unknown values where there are any missing instances\n   746→\t\t\tfor i, v := range vals {\n   747→\t\t\t\tif v == cty.NilVal {\n   748→\t\t\t\t\tvals[i] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n   749→\t\t\t\t}\n   750→\t\t\t}\n   751→\t\t\tret = cty.TupleVal(vals)\n   752→\t\t} else {\n   753→\t\t\tret = cty.EmptyTupleVal\n   754→\t\t}\n   755→\n   756→\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n   757→\t\tvals := make(map[string]cty.Value)\n   758→\t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n   759→\t\t\tstrKey, ok := key.(addrs.StringKey)\n   760→\t\t\tif !ok {\n   761→\t\t\t\t// old key that is being dropped and not used for evaluation\n   762→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   763→\t\t\t}\n   764→\t\t\tvals[string(strKey)] = instance\n   765→\t\t}\n   766→\n   767→\t\tif len(vals) > 0 {\n   768→\t\t\t// We use an object rather than a map here because resource schemas\n   769→\t\t\t// may include dynamically-typed attributes, which will then cause\n   770→\t\t\t// each instance to potentially have a different runtime type even\n   771→\t\t\t// though they all conform to the static schema.\n   772→\t\t\tret = cty.ObjectVal(vals)\n   773→\t\t} else {\n   774→\t\t\tret = cty.EmptyObjectVal\n   775→\t\t}\n   776→\n   777→\tdefault:\n   778→\t\tval, ok := instances[addrs.NoKey]\n   779→\t\tif !ok {\n   780→\t\t\t// if the instance is missing, insert an unknown value\n   781→\t\t\tval = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n   782→\t\t}\n   783→\n   784→\t\tret = val\n   785→\t}\n   786→\n   787→\treturn ret, diags\n   788→}\n   789→\n   790→func (d *evaluationStateData) getEphemeralResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   791→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   792→\n   793→\tif d.Operation == walkValidate || d.Operation == walkEval {\n   794→\t\t// Ephemeral instances are never live during the validate walk. Eval is\n   795→\t\t// similarly offline, and since there is no value stored we can't return\n   796→\t\t// anything other than dynamic.\n   797→\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral), diags\n   798→\t}\n   799→\n   800→\t// Now, we're going to build up a value that represents the resource\n   801→\t// or resources that are in the state.\n   802→\tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\n   803→\n   804→\t// First, we're going to load any instances that we have written into the\n   805→\t// deferrals system. 908→}\n   909→\n   910→func (d *evaluationStateData) GetOutput(addr addrs.OutputValue, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   911→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   912→\n The graph walk gradually registers the\n\t// set of instances for each object within the graph nodes for those\n\t// objects, and so as long as the graph has been built correctly the\n\t// set of instances for an object should always be available by the time\n\t// we're evaluating expressions that refer to it.\n\tInstances *instances.Expander\n\n\t// NamedValues is where we keep the values of already-evaluated input\n\t// variables, local values, and output values.\n\tNamedValues *namedvals.State\n\n\t// EphemeralResources tracks the currently-open instances of any ephemeral\n\t// resources.\n\tEphemeralResources *ephemeral.Resources\n\n\t// Deferrals tracks resources and modules that have had either their\n\t// expansion or their specific planned actions deferred to a future\n\t// plan/apply round.\n\tDeferrals *deferring.Deferred\n\n\t// Plugins is the library of available plugin components (providers and\n\t// provisioners) that we have available to help us evaluate expressions\n\t// that interact with plugin-provided objects.\n\t//\n\t// From this we only access the schemas of the plugins, and don't otherwise\n\t// interact with plugin instances.\n\tPlugins *contextPlugins\n\n\t// State is the current state, embedded in a wrapper that ensures that\n\t// it can be safely accessed and modified concurrently.\n\tState *states.SyncState\n\n\t// Changes is the set of proposed changes, embedded in a wrapper that\n\t// ensures they can be safely accessed and modified concurrently.\n\tChanges *plans.ChangesSync\n\n\tPlanTimestamp time.Time\n}\n\n// Scope creates an evaluation scope for the given module path and optional\n// resource.\n//\n// If the \"self\" argument is nil then the \"self\" object is not available\n// in evaluated expressions. suggestion)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared local value`,\n\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`A local value with the name %q has not been declared.%s`, addr.Name, suggestion),\n\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n\n\tval := d.Evaluator.NamedValues.GetLocalValue(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath))\n\treturn val, diags\n}\n\nfunc (d *evaluationStateData) GetModule(addr addrs.ModuleCall, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\t// Output results live in the module that declares them, which is one of\n\t// the child module instances of our current module path.\n\tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath.Module().Child(addr.Name)\n\tabsAddr := addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n\n\tparentCfg := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendantForInstance(d.ModulePath)\n\tcallConfig, ok := parentCfg.Module.ModuleCalls[addr.Name]\n\tif !ok {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared module`,\n\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`The configuration contains no %s.`, moduleAddr),\n\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n\n\t// We'll consult the configuration to see what output names we are\n\t// expecting, so we can ensure the resulting object is of the expected\n\t// type even if our data is incomplete for some reason.\n\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.Descendant(moduleAddr)\n\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n\t\t// should never happen, since we have a valid module call above, this\n\t\t// should be caught during static validation.\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"output value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n\t}\n\toutputConfigs := moduleConfig.Module.Outputs\n\n\t// We don't do instance expansion during validation, and so we need to\n\t// return an unknown value. Technically we should always return\n\t// cty.DynamicVal here because the final value during plan will always\n\t// be an object or tuple type with unpredictable attributes/elements,\n\t// but because we never actually carry values forward from validation to\n\t// planning we lie a little here and return unknown list and map types,\n\t// just to give us more opportunities to catch author mistakes during\n\t// validation.\n\t//\n\t// This means that in practice any expression that refers to a module\n\t// call must be written to be valid for either a collection type or\n\t// structural type of similar kind, so that it can be considered as\n\t// valid during both the validate and plan walks.\n\tif d.Operation == walkValidate {\n\t\tatys := make(map[string]cty.Type, len(outputConfigs))\n\t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n\t\t\tatys[name] = cty.DynamicPseudoType // output values are dynamically-typed\n\t\t}\n\t\tinstTy := cty.Object(atys)\n\n\t\tswitch {\n\t\tcase callConfig.Count != nil:\n\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.List(instTy)), diags\n\t\tcase callConfig.ForEach != nil:\n\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(cty.Map(instTy)), diags\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(instTy), diags\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// For all other walk types, we proceed to dynamic evaluation of individual\n\t// instances, using the global instance expander. An earlier graph node\n\t// should always have registered the expansion of this module call before\n\t// we get here, unless there's a bug in the graph builders.\n\tallInstances := d.Evaluator.Instances\n\tinstKeyType, instKeys, known := allInstances.ExpandAbsModuleCall(absAddr)\n\tif !known {\n\t\t// If we don't know which instances exist then we can't really predict\n\t\t// anything at all. We can't even predict the return type based on\n\t\t// instKeyType because output values are dynamically-typed and so\n\t\t// our final result will always be an object or tuple type whose\n\t\t// attribute/element count we cannot predict.\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n\n\tinstanceObjVal := func(instKey addrs.InstanceKey) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\t\t// This function must always return a valid value, even if it's\n\t\t// just a cty.DynamicVal placeholder accompanying error diagnostics.\n\t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\t\tnamedVals := d.Evaluator.NamedValues\n\t\tmoduleInstAddr := absAddr.Instance(instKey)\n\t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(outputConfigs))\n\t\tfor name := range outputConfigs {\n\t\t\toutputAddr := moduleInstAddr.OutputValue(name)\n\n\t\t\t// Although we do typically expect the graph dependencies to\n\t\t\t// ensure that values get registered before they are needed,\n\t\t\t// we track depedencies with specific output values where\n\t\t\t// possible, instead of with entire module calls, and so\n\t\t\t// in this specific case it's valid for some of this call's\n\t\t\t// output values to not be known yet, with the graph builder\n\t\t\t// being responsible for making sure that no expression\n\t\t\t// in the configuration can actually observe that.\n\t\t\tif !namedVals.HasOutputValue(outputAddr) {\n\t\t\t\tattrs[name] = cty.DynamicVal\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\toutputVal := namedVals.GetOutputValue(outputAddr)\n\t\t\tattrs[name] = outputVal\n\t\t}\n\n\t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n\t}\n\n\tswitch instKeyType {\n\n\tcase addrs.NoKeyType:\n\t\t// In this case we should always have exactly one instance that\n\t\t// is addrs.NoKey. If not then there's a bug in the [instances.Expander]\n\t\t// implementation.\n\t\tif len(instKeys) != 1 {\n\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"module call has no instance key type but has %d instances (should be 1)\", len(instKeys)))\n\t\t}\n\t\tret, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKeys[0])\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\t\treturn ret, diags\n\n\tcase addrs.IntKeyType:\n\t\t// We can assume that the instance keys are in ascending numerical order\n\t\t// and are consecutive, per the contract of allInstances.ExpandModuleCall.\n\t\telems := make([]cty.Value, 0, len(instKeys))\n\t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n\t\t\telems = append(elems, instVal)\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn cty.TupleVal(elems), diags\n\n\tcase addrs.StringKeyType:\n\t\tattrs := make(map[string]cty.Value, len(instKeys))\n\t\tfor _, instKey := range instKeys {\n\t\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := instanceObjVal(instKey)\n\t\t\tattrs[string(instKey.(addrs.StringKey))] = instVal\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn cty.ObjectVal(attrs), diags\n\n\tdefault:\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  `Unsupported instance key type`,\n\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t`Module call %s has instance key type %#v, which is not supported by the expression evaluator. This is a bug in Terraform.`,\n\t\t\t\tabsAddr, instKeyType,\n\t\t\t),\n\t\t\tSubject: rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (d *evaluationStateData) GetResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\t// First we'll consult the configuration to see if an resource of this\n\t// name is declared at all.\n\tmoduleAddr := d.ModulePath\n\tmoduleConfig := d.Evaluator.Config.DescendantForInstance(moduleAddr)\n\tif moduleConfig == nil {\n\t\t// should never happen, since we can't be evaluating in a module\n\t\t// that wasn't mentioned in configuration.\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"resource value read from %s, which has no configuration\", moduleAddr))\n\t}\n\n\tconfig := moduleConfig.Module.ResourceByAddr(addr)\n\tif config == nil {\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  `Reference to undeclared resource`,\n\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(`A resource %q %q has not been declared in %s`, addr.Type, addr.Name, moduleDisplayAddr(moduleAddr)),\n\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n\n\t// Much of this function was written before we had factored out the handling\n\t// of instance keys into the separate instance expander model, and so it\n\t// does a bunch of instance-related work itself below.\n\t//\n\t// Currently, unknown instance keys are only possible when planning with\n\t// DeferralAllowed set to true in the PlanOpts, which should only be the\n\t// case in the stacks runtime (not the \"normal terraform\" modules runtime).\n\t// Thus, we have some amount of duplicated code remaining, to be more\n\t// certain that stacks-specific behaviors won't leak out into the standard\n\t// runtime.\n\t//\n\t// TODO: When deferred actions are more stable and robust in stacks, it\n\t// would be nice to rework this function to rely on the ResourceInstanceKeys\n\t// result for _all_ of its work, rather than continuing to duplicate a bunch\n\t// of the logic we've tried to encapsulate over ther already.\n\tif d.Operation == walkPlan || d.Operation == walkApply {\n\t\tif _, _, hasUnknownKeys := d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys(addr.Absolute(moduleAddr)); !hasUnknownKeys {\n\t\t\t// There really isn't anything interesting we can do in this situation,\n\t\t\t// because it means we have an unknown for_each/count, in which case\n\t\t\t// we can't even predict what the result type will be because it\n\t\t\t// would be either an object or tuple type decided based on the instance\n\t\t\t// keys.\n\t\t\t// (We can't get in here for a single-instance resource because in that\n\t\t\t// case we would know that there's only one key and it's addrs.NoKey,\n\t\t\t// so we'll fall through to the other logic below.)\n\t\t\tunknownVal := cty.DynamicVal\n\n\t\t\t// If an ephemeral resource is deferred we need to mark the returned unknown value as ephemeral\n\t\t\tif addr.Mode == addrs.EphemeralResourceMode {\n\t\t\t\tunknownVal = unknownVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn unknownVal, diags\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Build the provider address from configuration, since we may not have\n\t// state available in all cases.\n\t// We need to build an abs provider address, but we can use a default\n\t// instance since we're only interested in the schema.\n\tschema := d.getResourceSchema(addr, config.Provider)\n\tif schema == nil {\n\t\t// This shouldn't happen, since validation before we get here should've\n\t\t// taken care of it, but we'll show a reasonable error message anyway.\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\tSummary:  `Missing resource type schema`,\n\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"No schema is available for %s in %s. This is a bug in Terraform and should be reported.\", addr, config.Provider),\n\t\t\tSubject:  rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t}\n\tty := schema.ImpliedType()\n\n\tif addr.Mode == addrs.EphemeralResourceMode {\n\t\t// FIXME: This does not yet work with deferrals, and it would be nice to\n\t\t// find some way to refactor this so that the following code is not so\n\t\t// tethered to the current implementation details. Instead we should\n\t\t// have an abstract idea of first determining what instances the\n\t\t// resource has (using d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys) and\n\t\t// then retrieving the value for each instance to assemble into the\n\t\t// result, using some per-resource-mode logic maintained elsewhere.\n\t\treturn d.getEphemeralResource(addr, rng)\n\t}\n\n\trs := d.Evaluator.State.Resource(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath))\n\n\tif rs == nil {\n\t\tswitch d.Operation {\n\t\tcase walkPlan, walkApply:\n\t\t\t// During plan and apply as we evaluate each removed instance they\n\t\t\t// are removed from the working state. Since we know there are no\n\t\t\t// instances, return an empty container of the expected type.\n\t\t\tswitch {\n\t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyTupleVal, diags\n\t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.EmptyObjectVal, diags\n\t\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t\t// While we can reference an expanded resource with 0\n\t\t\t\t// instances, we cannot reference instances that do not exist.\n\t\t\t\t// Due to the fact that we may have direct references to\n\t\t\t\t// instances that may end up in a root output during destroy\n\t\t\t\t// (since a planned destroy cannot yet remove root outputs), we\n\t\t\t\t// need to return a dynamic value here to allow evaluation to\n\t\t\t\t// continue.\n\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] unknown instance %q referenced during %s\", addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath), d.Operation)\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\tcase walkImport:\n\t\t\t// Import does not yet plan resource changes, so new resources from\n\t\t\t// config are not going to be found here. Once walkImport fully\n\t\t\t// plans resources, this case should not longer be needed.\n\t\t\t// In the single instance case, we can return a typed unknown value\n\t\t\t// for the instance to better satisfy other expressions using the\n\t\t\t// value. This of course will not help if statically known\n\t\t\t// attributes are expected to be known elsewhere, but reduces the\n\t\t\t// number of problematic configs for now.\n\t\t\t// Unlike in plan and apply above we can't be sure the count or\n\t\t\t// for_each instances are empty, so we return a DynamicVal. We\n\t\t\t// don't really have a good value to return otherwise -- empty\n\t\t\t// values will fail for direct index expressions, and unknown\n\t\t\t// Lists and Maps could fail in some type unifications.\n\t\t\tswitch {\n\t\t\tcase config.Count != nil:\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t\t\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(ty), diags\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t// We should only end up here during the validate walk (or\n\t\t\t// console/eval), since later walks should have at least partial\n\t\t\t// states populated for all resources in the configuration.\n\t\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal, diags\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Now, we're going to build up a value that represents the resource\n\t// or resources that are in the state.\n\tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\n\n\t// First, we're going to load any instances that we have written into the\n\t// deferrals system. A deferred resource overrides anything that might be\n\t// in the state for the resource, so we do this first.\n\tfor key, value := range d.Evaluator.Deferrals.GetDeferredResourceInstances(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)) {\n\t\tinstances[key] = value\n\t}\n\n\t// Decode all instances in the current state\n\tpendingDestroy := d.Operation == walkDestroy\n\tfor key, is := range rs.Instances {\n\t\tif _, ok := instances[key]; ok {\n\t\t\t// Then we've already loaded this instance from the deferrals so\n\t\t\t// we'll just ignore it being in state.\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\t// Otherwise, we'll load the instance from state.\n\n\t\tif is == nil || is.Current == nil {\n\t\t\t// Assume we're dealing with an instance that hasn't been created yet.\n\t\t\tinstances[key] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tinstAddr := addr.Instance(key).Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n\t\tchange := d.Evaluator.Changes.GetResourceInstanceChange(instAddr, addrs.NotDeposed)\n\t\tif change != nil {\n\t\t\t// Don't take any resources that are yet to be deleted into account.\n\t\t\t// If the referenced resource is CreateBeforeDestroy, then orphaned\n\t\t\t// instances will be in the state, as they are not destroyed until\n\t\t\t// after their dependants are updated.\n\t\t\tif change.Action == plans.Delete {\n\t\t\t\tif !pendingDestroy {\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Planned resources are temporarily stored in state with empty values,\n\t\t// and need to be replaced by the planned value here.\n\t\tif is.Current.Status == states.ObjectPlanned {\n\t\t\tif change == nil {\n\t\t\t\t// FIXME: This is usually an unfortunate case where we need to\n\t\t\t\t// lookup an individual instance referenced via \"self\" for\n\t\t\t\t// postconditions which we know exists, but because evaluation\n\t\t\t\t// must always get the resource in aggregate some instance\n\t\t\t\t// changes may not yet be registered.\n\t\t\t\tinstances[key] = cty.DynamicVal\n\t\t\t\t// log the problem for debugging, since it may be a legitimate error we can't catch\n\t\t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[WARN] instance %s is marked as having a change pending but that change is not recorded in the plan\", instAddr)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tinstances[key] = change.After\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tios, err := is.Current.Decode(ty)\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t// This shouldn't happen, since by the time we get here we\n\t\t\t// should have upgraded the state data already.\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Invalid resource instance data in state\",\n\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Instance %s data could not be decoded from the state: %s.\", instAddr, err),\n\t\t\t\tSubject:  &config.DeclRange,\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tval := ios.Value\n\n\t\tinstances[key] = val\n\t}\n\n\t// ret should be populated with a valid value in all cases below\n\tvar ret cty.Value\n\n\tswitch {\n\tcase config.Count != nil:\n\t\t// figure out what the last index we have is\n\t\tlength := -1\n\t\tfor key := range instances {\n\t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif int(intKey) >= length {\n\t\t\t\tlength = int(intKey) + 1\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif length > 0 {\n\t\t\tvals := make([]cty.Value, length)\n\t\t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n\t\t\t\tintKey, ok := key.(addrs.IntKey)\n\t\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\t\t// old key from state, which isn't valid for evaluation\n\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t\tvals[int(intKey)] = instance\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t// Insert unknown values where there are any missing instances\n\t\t\tfor i, v := range vals {\n\t\t\t\tif v == cty.NilVal {\n\t\t\t\t\tvals[i] = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tret = cty.TupleVal(vals)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tret = cty.EmptyTupleVal\n\t\t}\n\n\tcase config.ForEach != nil:\n\t\tvals := make(map[string]cty.Value)\n\t\tfor key, instance := range instances {\n\t\t\tstrKey, ok := key.(addrs.StringKey)\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\t// old key that is being dropped and not used for evaluation\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tvals[string(strKey)] = instance\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif len(vals) > 0 {\n\t\t\t// We use an object rather than a map here because resource schemas\n\t\t\t// may include dynamically-typed attributes, which will then cause\n\t\t\t// each instance to potentially have a different runtime type even\n\t\t\t// though they all conform to the static schema.\n\t\t\tret = cty.ObjectVal(vals)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tret = cty.EmptyObjectVal\n\t\t}\n\n\tdefault:\n\t\tval, ok := instances[addrs.NoKey]\n\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t// if the instance is missing, insert an unknown value\n\t\t\tval = cty.UnknownVal(ty)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tret = val\n\t}\n\n\treturn ret, diags\n}\n\nfunc (d *evaluationStateData) getEphemeralResource(addr addrs.Resource, rng tfdiags.SourceRange) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\tif d.Operation == walkValidate || d.Operation == walkEval {\n\t\t// Ephemeral instances are never live during the validate walk. Eval is\n\t\t// similarly offline, and since there is no value stored we can't return\n\t\t// anything other than dynamic.\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral), diags\n\t}\n\n\t// Now, we're going to build up a value that represents the resource\n\t// or resources that are in the state.\n\tinstances := map[addrs.InstanceKey]cty.Value{}\n\n\t// First, we're going to load any instances that we have written into the\n\t// deferrals system. A deferred resource overrides anything that might be\n\t// in the state for the resource, so we do this first.\n\tfor key, value := range d.Evaluator.Deferrals.GetDeferredResourceInstances(addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)) {\n\t\tinstances[key] = value\n\t}\n\n\tabsAddr := addr.Absolute(d.ModulePath)\n\tkeyType, keys, haveUnknownKeys := d.Evaluator.Instances.ResourceInstanceKeys(absAddr)\n\tif haveUnknownKeys {\n\t\t// We can probably do better than totally unknown at least for a\n\t\t// single-instance resource, but we'll just keep it simple for now.\n\t\t// Result must be marked as ephemeral so that we can still catch\n\t\t// attempts to use the results in non-ephemeral locations, so that\n\t\t// the operator doesn't end up trapped with an error on a subsequent\n\t\t// plan/apply round.\n\t\treturn cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral), diags\n\t}\n\n\tephems := d.Evaluator.EphemeralResources\n\tgetInstValue := func(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\t\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n\t\t// If we have a deferred instance with this key we don't need to check if it is live or not,\n\t\t// it has not been created so we can just return the deferred value.\n\t\tif v, ok := instances[addr.Resource.Key]; ok {\n\t\t\treturn v, diags\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tval, isLive := ephems.InstanceValue(addr)\n\t\tif !isLive {\n\t\t\t// If the instance is no longer \"live\" by the time we're accessing\n\t\t\t// it then that suggests that it needed renewal and renewal has\n\t\t\t// failed, and so the object's value is no longer usable. We'll\n\t\t\t// still return the value in case it's somehow useful for diagnosis,\n\t\t\t// but we return an error to prevent further evaluation of whatever\n\t\t\t// other expression depended on the liveness of this object.\n\t\t\t//\n\t\t\t// This error message is written on the assumption that it will\n\t\t\t// always appear alongside the provider's renewal error, but that'll\n\t\t\t// be exposed only once the (now-zombied) ephemeral resource is\n\t\t\t// eventually closed, so that we can avoid returning the same error\n\t\t\t// multiple times.\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\tSummary:  \"Ephemeral resource instance has expired\",\n\t\t\t\tDetail: fmt.Sprintf(\n\t\t\t\t\t\"The remote object for %s is no longer available due to a renewal error, so Terraform cannot evaluate this expression.\",\n\t\t\t\t\taddr,\n\t\t\t\t),\n\t\t\t\tSubject: rng.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t}\n\t\tif val == cty.NilVal {\n\t\t\tval = cty.DynamicVal.Mark(marks.Ephemeral)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn val, diags\n\t}\n\n\tswitch keyType {\n\tcase addrs.NoKeyType:\n\t\t// For \"no key\" we're returning just a single object representing\n\t\t// the single instance of this resource.\n\t\tinstVal, moreDiags := getInstValue(absAddr.Instance(addrs.NoKey))\n\t\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\t\treturn instVal,
